When stomach pain originates in the kidneys and is accompanied by swelling, and it affects women differently, then it's necessary to apply the cautery on both sides of the kidneys and also to use the wrist cautery that we have described; and if we cauterize in the middle, one will do three lines of cauterization, and they will provide more assistance.
de la vessie	From the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is swollen and weak from heat and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then instruct for a cautery in the lower part of the bladder, where the body hair begins near the fingers. On each hand (right and left), and let each cautery be as long as the distance of one hand; and make one cautery behind the back, or two if needed; and let the cauteries follow the outline described beforehand.
de la marris	From the marrows
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers (likely referring to menstrual cycles) are corrupted and their periods delayed; and when they come in, one feels great pain: therefore, it should be that you perform three cauterizations inside the uterus, as we have said about the bladder cautery, and two cauterizations behind the back; let the cauterizations follow the outline described previously.
de la hainche	From the thigh
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the oily fluids descend to the socket of the thigh, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the leg is longer than the other when measured together; and you find the bones at their origin points visible, then you should apply a cautery on the socket of the thigh with an appearance like one half of a circle, and mark in front of the bone inside the socket as it turns, so that the socket remains within the circle; and if you make the cauterizations like those made to the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you don't have access to such cauterizations, make three large ones from the olive oil, and make sure each cauterization is as perfect as all the rest; and treat it until it heals.
de la dolor de la hainche	Regarding the pain in the thigh
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the thigh bone, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and patients are treated as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not work, and the disease is old: then you should cleanse the patient of the large humors using putrid pills or other beneficial similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After performing the cautery; and regarding the manner of the cautery, it follows two manners: that is to say, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery follows several methods, among which one is like this: you should cauterize at the hip bone with three triangular cauteries according to this form. Each must have a good depth and size large enough, and there's space of the width of two thumbs between each cautery. The shape of these cauteries is that of an olive; never make a cauterization in the middle of the upper part of the hip bone because following this pattern results in four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see fit, when cauterizing with the circular cautery as we have described in the dislocation of the thigh bone; but do it this way that all the thigh is contained within the circles, and every part of the knee's skin be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is how it's done in sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and doesn't reach up to the thigh or down to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it extends up to the thigh and leg, make two fire cauteries there where the patient says pain holds them back, and add three above the ankle, on the left side a little bit; and use knife-like cauterization techniques, and scorch off any thickened skin around the wound. And if the patient feels the pain spreading down to knee or almost at its knee, apply the cautery where he feels the pain for three or four points of heat, considering these as "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if more work is needed, then do it; and if it appears that the pain lies between the knee and thigh, then perform cauterization with a surgical or circular instrument. Be well guarded in all your cauterizations making sure not to leave them incomplete until you burn nerves and large arteries, and do not cause the patient more harm and contraction than necessary.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen several cases where cautery was done on the ankle up to the knee, and it was only stopped when the leg was completely swollen, and also all the toes, and they were pierced and corrupted entirely.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal treatment that led to death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, apply a cautery to both areas, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men spoke about the fire cautery for the hip, as follows: make it like this kind of iron, and let its size be as thick as one's little finger or a bit less, and have it with joints in between and place the joints starting from one part to the other of space equivalent to the length of a handkerchief; and let the joints be divided into two parts each, and they should also resemble knots, and there should be an iron rod well made; this is its shape.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it's completely red and smokes emit, then place it on the spot of the hip disease, and twist over the healthy side; and apply one application of this cautery once and leave it for three days; and after that, apply a poultice of butter, and keep the wound open long; cure with ointment until it heals.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery for the fear of his judgment, and we rarely see it being used; nonetheless, this is a good type of cautery, which one can tolerate, and leaves where it appears.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The medical hot cauteries consist of an instrument with joints through which the edge descends within the door. It should be made of steel or iron that is long on one side and has two knuckles at the top, with each having the thickness equivalent to a small bone in between. They should also have a flat surface from above and join together following this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After positioning on the hip of the lying patient toward his sound side, and quickly place your hand close to the hip bone; next pour a small amount of hot ash between the two circles which has been heated by fire, and let it stay for an hour while allowing the patient to endure the heat and burn.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it also finds a bite as with fire; and when the biting passes, raise your hand along with the tool and gently lift the hip from the ash. Leave this for three days, and apply butter until that which is blackened by the scorching dries out; and let it be for three days while putrefaction takes effect. This would then be considered the second aid after the treatment of ointments when the patient is healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread up to the thigh or even down to the leg, you should make the instrument that pierces according to what you have done in the buttock area; and this is the method of the hot needle, which I have written about in the section dealing with correcting medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take an equal amount of alum and live chalk, as much of one as the other, grind them together, and put them in a new jar.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Let it have the small blade of a razor so that its point can enter; and place that jar in another well-sealed jar, and put alum and chalk and gentle heat underneath, until there is twice as much above the powders than you will take with your hand; and leave it like this until the heat produces water vapor and sediment or till the contents are fully heated. Then take all of that substance, and pour it over chalk and on top of the alum so as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And indeed it will be much useful and administered in the process of medical operations and fire cauteries on other limbs. For they perform work akin to fire's actions, and are applied with other medicines like tannisine and anacardi, honey, chaldron mixed with soap; all these things combined together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment that some nobles were subjected to for the pain in their hip and sciatic nerve, and he says much about it, and states that no other treatment was done, and that they became well all at once when this treatment was applied. And he recommends bathing as he instructs later on in this manner.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And it instructs in this way: take some pure green and dried litargite, crush it finely with a little fat, mix it thoroughly and place it on the hip, thigh and leg where the pain is felt. Then bind it on; let it stay for three hours, and ensure that no longer do you feel any burning sensation due to the application of this ointment.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make them enter into a bath as their body becomes somewhat revived, and have them lie down, and the pain will leave them entirely and they will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	Know that no one should use such medicines with a cautery, unless after the removal of the body's essence.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides states that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with donkey's blood, if it helps not at all; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take ash and mix it with old oil, then place it on the depression located between the base of the thumb and another one called the instep.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking donkey hair, dry it and hold it over the flame until it becomes charcoal. Place it on the ash, let it stay until it turns black; and do this again several times, without stopping until you think by sense that it reaches to the hip bone and the pain is relieved. This method of cautery is called "donkey hair cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or from percussion or due to an excess of evacuation, or due to any likeness of cold matter spread out, none of these likenesses warrant cauterization, because it is something that comes from the introduction of cold matter into the body.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary to do this after the body has been emptied of fetid pills or other likenesses, by placing marks on the back at the place where the pain is felt, three lines with an 'enche' symbol in each line, and in each line more than .v. cauterizations according to the virtue and quantity that the body can endure; and perform the cauterization using the type of cautery called 'points'; and if you see fit, do three or four cauterizations on the middle one in this pattern:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often affects young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they become faint when they stand up and fear. And you find that in the last spine at the back and on us the appearance that comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you watch it being treated,
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery burns each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see this, apply the fire cautery between the vertebrae at the place where it burns two or three lines in, and make sure the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the healing is complete as long as it is clean according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply the cautery in pus which is in the area of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture spreading throughout each limb, and when pain appears in the feet, which they call "gout" properly, and when it is due to cold reasons and treated with medicines that cannot cure it, then treatment involves using cautery in this manner: make the shape of the cautery around the joint of the foot, and have the olive oil cautery look like this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you touch on the side of the leg near the foot, if you make the cautery across the entire cautery saying "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains extend up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, if you need to apply the cautery on each knee three or four across each part, for the entire olive oil coated area; and if you need more, do so more, but don't remove your hand until the skin under the heat is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knees and back, then administer the cautery that we said in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points between the inner wrist lines; and if there remains no pain on the wrists, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and take medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if you give him good care and cleanse phlegm, he will recover with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the syphilitic sore
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When division comes about in anger, and the veins descend into the intestines it is newly so, you should know that when you are curing him or her, do not eat meat for that day; and use things that lighten the stomach, so that the wind descends from his or her abdomen. After that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to cut his fat until the veins repair themselves, then take them with your fingers, and examine around the division above the bone in the hand's wrist, and at every sign it should be similar to half a circle from above the chest; then heat up the cautery which is described here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	Until it is white and discharges pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the boils at their source; and have the attendants shave his hand so it doesn't turn back; and work well on the thighs for the patient, and apply one over him to keep them in place under his thighs, and another under his buttocks where they can shave his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign on all your hand, and hold it straight until you touch the bone, and if you don't reach the bone on the first try, repeat once more until you get there; and be subtle that the boil doesn't spill when you do the cautery; so as not to burn them; and by this way the patients should not die or suffer from other maladies.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach to the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their size, and also those for adults as large according to their measure; after three days apply wax ointment with the fire cauterizer until the scab is removed; after this application of other dressings until it heals properly, and let them lie forty days on their back so that the wound is well sealed; and these instructions should be followed for a long time, so that when they wish to go into rooms the boils do not burst.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when they want to get up, they should use a well-made bandage and wear it for another forty days; and have good rest, work little and guard against overeating and drinking too much, as well as not shouting too loud; and once he follows this advice, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say after the treatment of the tailor in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	And when wounds come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then I will have the fire cautery done according to its quantity with each application, and perhaps use one-third of the full dose; after treating it according to what we have said; and none of the old ones said that one should apply the heat of the cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But the first sign is the location of the entrance and draw a line across the width above the wound, and another below, and hold your hand with the entire blade of the cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first applications of the cauterization are lighter and more moist.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in no limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	And when pain comes to any limb, due to falling or being struck, and that pain lasts for a long time, and medicine does not help in treating it, then it should be cauterized using the fire cautery known as "points", with applications of the cautery according to the length of the member, its smallness, its weakness and its usefulness, as well as its position of twists and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it has healed after the first cautery, that's fine; if not, start another cautery on this one, because these kinds of burns should make the patient feel discomfort in the limb close to where they are applied, so you must perform the cauteries as long as the body is healing.
de meselerie	Of cautery by fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they pierce at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The patient is treated once with each cauterization by a great help, and similarly the disease comes from the putrefaction of humor and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can't you see the cauterizer? Please take care that if the disease is at the beginning, and it's treated according to what we have said in the division, without spreading or remaining there, and you doubt that the corruption would spread throughout the body, then do these cauterizations on the head: I move the head from one side to another nine times, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and II on the two horns, and I behind on the cheekbones; and let your hand stay as long as the cauterization reaches up to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the fumes of large humors can escape; and cauterize it lightly according to what was done previously.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the moisture is everywhere dispersed; and it is clearly absent, then you should cauterize with these cauterizing tools that we have mentioned: one on top of the nose, and two cauterizations on the spine at the neck, and six cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one big one over the buttocks and another down below, and two on the shoulders; and two around the knees, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of hands and feet, and in the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are behind the last toe, do not burn them. And never cauterize over bone at the elbow, and one more on the bone of the stomach, and one more on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I use a cautery, the more help it becomes, and benefits the patient; and know that patients do not feel pain from the cautery as healthy individuals would, for their body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it should be that the cautery is large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in ways of iron tools.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment, wash the affected area with flour mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but remains inflamed, then apply cauteries to the limb according to its size and the size of the limb; and let the cauteries penetrate a little into the edge of the wound. Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never does one perform cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the place where the nerve is that makes the limb move; and thus there must be an incision; and in no way should anyone interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the release points of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of cautery from fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is advanced, and medicine in its original form proves ineffective, then apply a small amount of cautery using a fire cautery, according to the quantity of the root being burned, until the white part emerges and changes color; then treat with flour mixed with lentils several times along with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood from rooster and blood from duck, each in one part; mix all together, wrap it with a cloth, and let it be exposed on the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for gangrene by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the ulcer begins and you see it stop, if you notice this, cauterize with the fire cautery around the entire circumference of the ulcer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And still the wise ones say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the ulcer; and yet I do not think this is good, for I fear it might cause the tissue to become damaged and decayed, and I have already decided never to do so again; and a more straightforward approach is that one should cauterize around, with the fire cautery which is called 'circular', as we described in the context of various cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the boil that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called 'adubelati', and it slowly progresses towards death due to overactivity or the excess caused by her, or as she ages with weakness (that is, being too old), and she has little blood, or because of tension; and you see that she is hastening to die: then cauterize internally using several small cauteries; after which leave it like this.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	And it will hasten towards death.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced right through with all the cautery, if you heat up this form of the cautery:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this illness called 'adubelati', while the cauteries have penetrated through its heart, and let these cauteries be such that they push out from within in such a way that the process of decay is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After you have treated it as long as it has been properly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire through iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another form of disease one encounters is called 'corrosive', and it is nothing else but a member infection for it destroys members as if the dry woods were being burned.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the body that can endure a fire cautery, then prepare your fire cauteries with small and large tongs according to where the disease is in the body; after cauterizing all around until you remove the entire corruption, and leave nothing behind, so that everything that has been corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And leave it for three days, and apply burning with oil on the treated areas until the dryness from the fire has healed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of ointments that produce flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days you see that the wound is healing well, this is good; and if not, then reapply the cautery to where it has remained on your shoulder from the corruption of the first one.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this method was sometimes treated with medicine instead of the fire cautery; but still, the fire cautery is more effective. I have already mentioned the treatment for the application of medicine elsewhere in my division: use it whenever you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of stones that come to stones
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Quite often, stones that emerge from within cause a sickness known as "cysts" according to our understanding, and it is a large lump that causes pain in the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this sickness are done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This means, you know, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery commands you to heat it just like a feather from a goose; make sure it is well made of good iron at the size that can hold the nail in all directions, and ensure there are delicate edges. After making it very hot on the nail, twist your hand around the stick fully until it reaches the end of the hole; and leave it like this for three days until it begins to produce gangrene; then have him make a dressing of ground wild onions mixed with oil, and let the dressing remain all night, and the nail will come out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with ointment until it is cleansed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they have turned on the inside of your arm and occur many times in hands and nails, it is necessary that you take a hot water cautery; and do this way: take a spider hair or iron, or a goose feather, and place them over the nail and the thistle, which means for warts. And put the rod where it turns everything around completely, then add a bit of hot water, and hold your hand well, pressing with your hand as you turn the edge of the rod to the root of the nail, and then find the deep passage of hot water all the way to the root; and let the patient endure the hot water bite for a little an hour; then leave it like this, and it will be uprooted from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So treat one after another, until you have treated all those within the body, then cleanse of growths that cause flesh.
li cure dou trembler	treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	And when someone shakes due to cold or nerves, or malaria fever or other conditions, it should be that you do this: apply three or four hot applications on the spine of the back, one hot application between each vertebra; and one application under the fingers and one at stomach with the olive cautery. If this doesn't stop shaking, then hasten the recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	pimple sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Every time visible from outside the body is bathed, or pus-filled ulcers that come from large corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	When they become visible at the start that one should do cautery on each tip of the pimple: a fine fire stick, whose tip is held in the flame, or from the root of long Aristolochia, or with the lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And each time they are cauterized at the beginning when they become visible, according to this manner, and they cannot grow into more before, but all excesses from which they come are removed, and it becomes healthy; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there have been great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound, or during the incision of an abscess, or with the cautery on the limb, and similar situations; and it is very unpleasant to smell this.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to no one, if you hurry to place your index finger on the cut of the vein, hold it there until the pulse ceases under your finger and no more drop escapes; then heat several olive oil cautery tools, both small and large, until they are all red hot. Then take one, or a large one depending on the size of the wound and its location where the artery is routed, and place the cautery over that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery in contact until the pulse has been extinguished.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are extinguished, then take one of another cautery that is heated quickly.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to apply this one after the other until the pulse has been extinguished completely; and beware that you do not burn the nerve underneath it, and that no harm comes upon the patient; know that when there is no beat of the artery, you cannot properly extinguish the pulse even if the artery is large, except through four methods as we have said: by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by strong tightening of a thread, or by medicines placed on which have the power to extinguish the blood; and bind it and hold it in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers bandaging tightly with cloths or places burning objects upon them, or other similar things, if it does not benefit, they should not do so.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if such an event occurs and there is no sight or medicine available, should place their finger upon the wound of the vein as we have said, and properly extend it until the coldness remains above the wound and above the vein; and they must not move it but moisten it with cool water often enough until it becomes very cold so long that the finger is frozen, swollen and remains cold; and apply cauteries and medicines where necessary.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments for amputations
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases where it is necessary to use a fire cautery or medicine cauter, and their uses, causes, instruments, and forms of cauterization; and we placed that chapter up until the knee, and I will proceed with this chapter in the same manner for those who find them more easily understandable.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than with the first uses of a cautery instrument, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often blood evacuation when opening veins, and incising abscesses, and treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and cutting into stones, among other things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I urge you to refrain from foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For few ways of people come into treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who have barely survived with their illness that they die lightly due to the ignorance they find in their disease, and the severity of their evil; and from this one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these ones who give their meaning and say: "Wait, I am okay"; and the illness is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not right that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but place more consideration in your honor than in your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely from what you are certain and can know; and use prediction and indication in treatments for the well-being of your patients; and this will help you gain good reputation, glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, our kings give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire from the holy inspiration of their hand, so be it.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or if I have organized this chapter by devising it in parts according to chapters, specifically regarding the sections on cauteries as I devised them from the head down to the feet, so that you will find it easier to understand what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes about very often in infants at birth, and when the mother restrains the head of the infant too tightly; and it happens not because of any known reason.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never see this disease in anyone other than children, and among all those I have seen, death came quickly; and because of this, it seems to me that I should stop the work with these kinds of treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw an infant of whom the shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day to such a degree that it could no longer bear it; and because of this moisture, he died. This moisture is assembled over the bone near the elbow, between the bone and the skin; and the surgical procedures are such that the moisture is between the bone and the skin, and the abscesses are small, causing you to cut into the head along a broad slit; and it goes as far as two inches in length while the moisture flows. And see here the shape of the suppuration:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If there is more moisture involved, and if the abscess is bigger, then make two incisions in a cross-like manner, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and if you see that the openings near the head on both sides are widened from each part, and the sharp pain increases when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not respond: then it is necessary to cut through the middle of the head with three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after making the incision, remove all moisture completely outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the cuts from cloths and powders, then I apply wine and oil, and leave it like this for five days; afterwards release him, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the head rest equally, then let the patient eat dried meat of the back of a wet animal until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the opening of the abscess is large, and the assembly of the water; for it is never in front; it is never behind; neither to the right; nor to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut the place where the abscess opens and fill with water, make a cut according to what you are able to do; and be careful not to sever an artery; look for blood flow, so that the patient dies due to bleeding and removal of moisture.
de reume	regarding the treatment
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or at the anus, and this illness is old, and the treatment with medicine does not help, then the last resort therapy would be the cauterization using which one severs those two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them recover, the patient should take off his head; after that, rub the back of one with a coarse cloth until the arteries are visible, then remove the patient's neck up to all the cloth. Then look where the vein lies, and on both sides after the ears, and they have come together; then mark the sides with an incision, then cut each side from an incising tool in two parts, until the cut reaches the bone, and do this by making cuts around the size of a large head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you can see it, hold the blade near the artery and cut above it, also making a cut as deep as two inches through it.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein has been cut, make sure that the blood flows continuously outwards at the top.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open upon feeling, it must be that you measure the size of the space up to three fingers, then press and push until reaching the bone; and what needs to be removed from blood is six c/ (approximately 3.6 liters), and by chance a little more or less according to how the patient can bear it, and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if it remains on the bone just above the cut point, if there's no abscess developing under the cut, then close the wound and bind it, and apply ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old age headaches and acute colds arise, due to the moisture from tears and heat in the temples and forehead area as well as similar symptoms, it is treated through various methods of medical treatment and none of these help. Therefore, we should remove the veins of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of their extraction is such that one should place themselves behind the hair on the temples of their patient and hear at the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well through its beating and responds only within some very cold men; and if it does respond, then restrain their neck by some cloths of theirs, then rub their head with a rough cloth, and raise their head in hot water until the artery appears clearly. Then take the spatula from which this is made:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you feel the artery, then take it up high with forceps, and remove all threads that are from each part; and if the artery is thin, cut it at the tip of the little finger, then cut out that part according to the size of two shoulders.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if she isn't cured, then neither will her child live fully at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain out six and seven times up to ten times; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with two thick silk threads for double strength so that decay does not occur before the welding of the wound, and it does not recur with bleeding; then remove the excess matter between those two threads at that time itself, and then, if you see fit, gently cauterize up to the bone with a small cautery tool until the heads are hollowed out; this is the completed work, if the patient does not have fever and has hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterizations are aid to finish off the wetnesses: because it is more great aid for the wetnesses.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that we fill the entire area with old cotton and place good tents on top; and when they are released, if you apply dry medicine-making substances that produce pus, as well as tents, until they become clean; and if there's a lack of a copper piece in the artery, you must do it like what you perform, hurry by cauterizing or use the area filled with vitriol and hold it tightly with your hand so the wound becomes dry; and if you don't have that tool at hand, insert a small amount into the cotton until the wound is frozen, and rinse the cotton in cold water until pus stops coming out, then hold it properly. And the one who is slower and lighter during the extraction of the artery should cauterize the skin of this cauterization trenching for two parts, but make sure the trenchings are well separated to last longer with heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the tools are too tight, it retains less of its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be between the two knives an inch of space, and then when you mark to close the two ends, and you place the hot iron up until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in both places; and they must be separated by about one inch because this cautery does not stick throughout completely; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are draining through veins above the neck bone at the head's back, and no benefit is received from the medicine being applied there, you'll see the skin turn red in response to it, and feel your forehead pulsate as if with a fever; and wherever they are damp and moist so that paper hairs fall off, and the papers heat up due to this, and are burned by the heat of the tears, then this treatment must be used.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they named the old "healer of burns", and if you treat a person with this illness, let them have hair on their head or forehead, then make three cuts evenly across the forehead according to its length; and make one cut halfway down along each side of the forehead, like two doves all in line from nose to mouth until they join at the corner, and the other two cuts are parallel to the sides through the paper-like skin. And beware not to cut the arteries that run above the skin; and keep your hand away from the continuation of both jaws, and each wound should be three inches wide across their joins; have a piece of sponge and some cloths ready to wipe off any blood, then use the sharp blade from one of these four corners they form.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	After making the cut behind the temple up to the second cut; and burn all the skin that is between the two cuts completely until it reaches the flesh above the bone. Then cut further along the middle cut up to the other end, and then remove this hot broth.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If there's a first cut in the opening made with the tool known as "cutter", and it is very sharp on one side, while on the other side it's blunt, not sharp, and this has the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And position the incision towards the soft tissue at the knee, and direct the cut towards the bone at the kneecap, and press the blade until it feels at the smallest fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And remove all the vessels that descend from the head as veins until the cut continues down to where it opens at the knee, and then do more cutting in the middle fissure up to the other opening; and then extract equal blood, express the wound for the taken blood; then place a piece of old cotton into each incision, and apply moist cloths soaked in wine and oil and garlic, and make sure not to let pus appear; and on the third day, release the stitches, and bring a large amount of water bathing, then administer a remedy with basilicum oil, and other remedies for wounds until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the pus
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When it comes to sudden catarrh (illness) accustomed to occur, and you see the eyes red and small, and weakening of vision, and burnt paper; and the hair is greasy, and one sweats profusely in fever, and the body shivers; then know by these occurrences that those substances and that catarrh do not come from many veins, and the moist cure that it is, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient behind his forehead, then make a large cut through the middle of the forehead, and another small one below.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the temple on the left to the temple on the right, and let the incision go until it reaches the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating; and when the bone is revealed, drain all the blood with a sponge, then clean inside the two lips of the incision and place old cotton between them, and lin fabric; then cover it with moist cloths soaked in wine and oil, and avoid removing any tissue; once removed, you should rub the bone until the root begins to appear, then cleanse it with things that dry out roots.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of coloflorence, and make a paste; and apply this paste to the wounds to promote flesh growth everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that is inserted into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or mine stones or similar things such as iron; or seed, such as beans, peas; or flowing matter such as water and air and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it closes in the ear hole or any other manner of thing that does not fit with the ear, and does not grow in the ear, place the ear under the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if any purple or saffron oil distills out, then proceed with extraction; and make them sneeze while holding a candle, and stuff their nostrils when they are sneezing, put pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and place the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	It often comes good through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then proceed with the removal by using fine needles, of which here is the form:

li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work involves taking the following steps: you should choose a fine needle and attach two threads of silk that are fine and strong. de la porriture de l’oil	Regarding the decay of the eye

dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the breaking of an oviductal membrane
