When disruption comes to the oviductal membrane, then opened, and brings out material like a grain of resin and is observable; thus if you see this coated, the organs are such that you can insert a needle at the root of the part below until it reaches above there, then insert another needle or with double thread from the part behind the bladder; and make the puncture, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut the part of the double thread and tie a portion of the membrane internally, and tightly stretch it, then remove the needle and place wool soaked in abundant egg on it; and let it until the thread and the membrane are both removed with the oviduct, then treat the eye with soothing substances until the wound is healed; and none of these times is the wound restrained by the membrane from each part of a circular piece of cloth until she is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show a large appearance, then pierce at the thin sinus which comes through the back of the eye, and drain the watery mucus and lower the eyes, and enter into them straight away; then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bowl of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is only due to bile that has accumulated in the liver, resembling descending sharpness, and it's not real pain; and the appearance of this work's way is for you to make the patient sit on the prepared seat and straight, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move him as much as you see bile coming above to your eyes; then let it be placed and doesn't descend and clear out light, observe the things inside the person just like they were supposed to; and if it doesn't descend immediately, know that it's pain, and if the descent of the bile isn't prepared as we've said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you are to have the afflicted person sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and cut into the corneal tissue beginning from the junction of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, as long as the bow exits; and when it has exited, pour in a hot, sharp water mixed with honey, or hot water that has been boiled with fenugreek, then apply another cure until she is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	From the tears of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the signs of heat in the division, and what needs to be pricked; so we operate according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the afflicted person sit between your crossed hands, away from light by the sun, and tie the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye on your left hand where the eyes are together, or on your right hand if the eyes are apart; then take in your right hand (if the eyes are together), the tool called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eyes are apart; then place the tip of the tool below the cornea by about a finger's width into the corner of the eye up to the part lower than the tear duct, then push the tool called "almagda" forcefully and turn your hand until it pierces through the corner of the eye, feeling that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the size of the path of almagda be at full length to the measure of the space which starts from the lid until the end of the darkness; and this is the cornea of the eye; you will see the bone in the paper through the clarity of the corneal tissue, then place the tool up to it or where the water is, then expel along another way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Let him feel this now, so he can see the surgeon before him and the instrument in his own eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a brief rest, and when the needle ascends the second vein, apply force with the tool. And when it's firmly in place and no longer rising, gently remove the pearl by twisting your hand back and forth; and then add a little powdered emerald water to the eye, removing what is inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place the ointment or wet wool in olive oil and plentifully with an egg, and bind it with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those that belong to our nature, let's apply common balm with plenty of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are people who have hard eyes, it is necessary that you take the tool called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And prick only the conjunctive, do not go too far in it but make him lie subtly. Then put on pearls, as we have said; and upon completion of the operation provide a doctor to the patient who sleeps, for he sleeps on his back with his eyes closed; and refrain from all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move your head neither to the right nor to the left, and tie him according to his position until the third day. Then release him in that dark house himself, and test his vision, and make sure he sees nothing, then again tie him until the seventh day; and it should not be done during the course of treatment or after the incision now, but you should do this because the needle has risen quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	The healing of abscesses comes about when you release the eye before the seventh day and apply a dressing to the one who relieves the abscess; and once it is alleviated, then release the eye and place an eyelid on its face for a few days, and remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leaves the house little by little, and adapts to its conditions; know that no pupils should interfere in such a situation.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	One came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that they used to pierce alum here, sucking out the fever, but still, I have never seen anyone like this in our land nor have I read about it in old books; and perhaps it is a new thing.

Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And these are the head of the four from this same subtlety, and the last one in three angular veins.
de la char sor le neis	from the nostril's wax
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	None of the times, or hens' eggs laid in different ways, among which some resemble scorpions with the feet of pies; and if there are such cases, or if it has a charred carcass of a red color, and if a carcass is soured of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this matter of those carcasses that are soured but not burned, you must have the patient lie between your hands facing the sun; work on their nostrils and sprinkle vinegar onto those carcasses, then remove them. Proceed with what you can bear up against the subtle sharp spittle on one side, until you know that this carcass is entirely ossified.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains no matter we cannot remove, if you open up to allow the use of all one instrument finely lightly, ensuring nothing stays; and should it not ascend, or pus appear, then seek it out as seems fit; and should these be malicious pus, act swiftly and apply heat until the pus is stopped and every hair is removed completely, then pour water or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	In its operation and with moisture reaching up to the palate, know that there is blood; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, which prevents tools from cutting: thus you must insert a thread of linen somewhat thick, tie it by hand, and leave an interval between each knot equal to one or less; then put the thread in the nose of the patient, through their power, pulling it so that it emerges inside the mouth; many times children perform this as a school task, and it is a simple thing for someone who wishes to do it; then hold the head coming out by the nose with one hand, and the other head coming out from the mouth with the other hand, and recognize each in turn observing us who are holding.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Follow this as you know that the new has corrupted that flesh, then pull out the child, bleed it and moisten the filth with Egyptian ointment, and place it back in front of the nose as before; follow this for three days or more, until the ointments dissolve all remaining rotten flesh; and then put a snail of opium under the nose for several days if it is sound, and if there are needs for dried medicines, you can use them; this is the form of the tool to purify the head, on which one distills oils and medicines or wine.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or arsenic, resembling an open lamp, like a rod, and guide him thus; and if you see fit, make a closed rod, and have your instrument filled for purging the head; and hold one end of the rod when you heat oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the nostril's wax
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times at the root of the nose a disease is born which is called 'telul', it grows and becomes large to see; and because this requires that you catch it at its beginning, then remove all bone, afterwards place in the middle the cautery or hot medicine; and if one delays catching it until it's big, they must beware if it's hard, changes color, loses sensation: don't touch it with iron as it is an infected abscess, for when you catch it once, it causes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is due to heat contact, not due to losing color, and you see that one can catch all of it, then empty the patient and treat the area with dry and restraining substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose has been treated and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come into one of these venous organs, it profits little, for in no men.

des apostemes des levres	removal of abscesses from lips

de la char des gencives	From the pulp of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, bone pieces arise on the gums that are attached, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with forceps and remove it to its root, allowing for bleeding or blood; then place it under vitriol powder, or other drying and restrictive powders; if this flesh returns after incision and many times occur, when you remove it again, cauterize it: if it doesn't return even after the cautery; these are the forms of instruments to remove it.
des sordens	Of cautering with fire, instruct the patient to allow the hairs to grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.

Some occasions are gathered at the root of the teeth within the mouth between the gums, and unpleasant and rough layers; and several times there is a black tooth with citrine stones and worms until the decay reaches the gum, and the teeth become stinking. Therefore, you need to hold the patient in your hands and have their head on the floor, and pull out the teeth or the scales that you see, as long as nothing remains; and then perform on the darkness and greenness, and yellowness and other tones until they are removed. And if what needs to be taken out is done at the first occasion, it's good; if not, start again the next day and the third day, until you have everything pulled out. Know that teeth require various types of instruments for pulling, according to what the work shows, because the scraper that pulls teeth from outside has different shapes than that which is pulled between the teeth; these shapes and others should be ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you delay removing it as long as possible, because one should not do this; because this is a very high material up to there therefore there should be no excuse for pulling.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is forced to endure treatment, it is necessary for you to be sure of your actions.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the patient, and watch that it is not a toothache, and make the good tooth bleed; and throughout this process never allow the pain to subside because until all the disease has been removed. We already have the desire to do this for these soldiers. And when you are certain about which tooth is causing the issue, then it's necessary to sear around the tooth up to two-thirds of its circumference in order to protect the gum from all sides; next move your hands or use delicate tweezers at the first pinch and pinch, until it is well separated, then firmly secure the tweezers. And have the head of the patient under the saint between your knees, and keep your hand still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the right tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out forcefully, take none of these tools and gently push them inside each part from both sides, and move it in the same way you did initially.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, you should fill it with sponges where they were; if you tightly extract it with forceps, make sure not to break it during extraction. It is important to carefully open inside the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure not to break it and leave a piece, and warn the patient about the greater pain from the root's mischief that comes after the initial one.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware not to do as the ignorant surgeons do, who break it once because of their haste and boldness, and don't provide them with what we have mentioned; but instead, they cause the same kind of disease to recur due to the roots that remain or the tooth that is broken. As often as this happens for diseases caused by an extraction. When you pull out the tooth, wash the mouth with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, wash the mouth with vitriol solution. If that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, with which you make your teeth first, should be long-pointed and have large handles, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may have large parts that do not bend during use, and they should be made of well-crafted iron, with teeth for holding them securely.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during extraction, it is necessary that you place wet cotton with butter inside for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the legs are softened, and I clamp the tongs known as 'alefri', making it seem like a properly cared-for bird's leg; they should also be done like a file and this is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to emerge from all these tongs, then you must uncover the flesh completely along the root and place an instrument which is called "althali", meaning palainche, as it appears in this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And make it hollow and thick so that it doesn't break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, it's good; if not, use all of the instruments, as their forms come after this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you have to help with this tool that has two points, as it appears in this form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other tools that are arranged in the proportion of teeth in front, and with this tool that seems like large pincers, as it appears in this form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be aware of this tool so it cannot break, and know that many tools of bone exist; similarly with other tools which are not named; and also skilled surgeons find their own instrument on their own according to what their tasks and diseases show them. For there are parts of diseases where the old did not teach any tools due to their variety; and if it breaks from carrying or another bone, or if it rots when it should remain solid, if they seek out the tool they need among those I've mentioned, and help through gestures, as shown here is its formation:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And may they be large and well holding to hold the bone, so it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return him to his place with medicines that suit this. And if there is decay in the bone and it is small, if he uses all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and it is ugly in shape, especially in maiden women, if you need to know whether the teeth have been born after the tooth and are not in their proper place, and cannot be worn or filed: then extract it; and if there is connection with the tooth, take this instrument as described here which resembles a pair of small hooks, and made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the bite is made little by little in my hands because of the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move others, and if it appears that one could shave it off, then I grind it with a piece of stone as shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it's also like the file used to make needles; and I grind the tooth slowly by hand lightly, so that it doesn't move until it finishes; then you level off at the end with a rasping tool, and if it's too sharp causing pain in the tongue, then you need to smooth out its roughness until it becomes even, so that it does not cause pain in the tongue nor damage speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is heated
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front is removed, or by percussion or by blow, and the patient cannot press against it what they eat until it chokes them; if they should be treated with medicated substances that restrict, and this does not work; then you must restrain it with a gold thread, as silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes. And let the gold thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see that they are overlapping the teeth, take the thread and double the handle between two healthy teeth, then place the diseased teeth between their teeth if there is one or more, until you feel it properly on the other side of the healthy tooth; then repeat the covering up to where you interrupted, and pull your hand gently but firmly until it does not move; and tie your wound at the root so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then twist the roots with a thread on tweezers, and join them together, placing them between healthy teeth, making sure not to irritate the tongue; and then leave it that way as tight as possible without causing discomfort. If it comes loose or the threads slip out, you may use another thread in their place; if it remains intact and serves this way for its entire duration, and this becomes the arrangement of the teeth and the position of the two healthy roots and the two remaining ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is removed, if it's placed back in its socket gradually, as we've said; and don't intervene with anything other than what you're instructed to do and can bear, and at no point make a form like an ox bone tooth, and place it in the socket where the defect is, then tighten it as we have described, and it stays and serves for as long as possible.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	None of the cords come from under the tongue or in their natural place at birth; or by accident from a healed wound. The procedures are such that you work on the mouth with the patient, having their head in your hand above them, and lift their tongue. Then twist the nerve cord until it's wide enough for the tongue to be dislodged from its position, and if there is hardness or swelling, this is due to a sudden wound healing, where you push out the hook and twist the nerve cord wide; and make sure not to let the incision go too deep as there might be an artery under it. And when you're done, you remove the patient from pinkish water or cold water, then place beneath the tongue a linen tent; and wipe down each night with antiseptic solution so that the wounds don't stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, put sulfur powder on the wound; and if it does not stop, cauterize with a slow-moving cautery which is good for this; then treat with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it to be of any color or blackness or hardness that the illness doesn't feel, do not touch it for it's a sore; and if it declines towards yellow fever, and there is moisture present, use the hook on it and cut with a fine incision from both sides, then release it on all sides; and if your wound doesn’t heal in your operation, place vinegar on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your operation as long as you apply force; then lift your head away from wetness and ease, and continue other treatments until it has healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	extraction of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No matter comes inside the throat cankers which are called 'godath', and they should be properly named as the two almonds. And when you treat them, just like what we have said in the division, if they do not heal, then take care: if it's hard pus of small sense and with a thread-like color, don't touch it even with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is big, don't touch it with iron even for bleeding; but leave it until it stops bleeding. Then you can remove it manually, or it would burst on its own. And if it's of a whitish color and the root is thin, have your tools ready to scoop out the pus, but first check if the pus clot is settled and calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the sick person sit in front of the sun, and let their limbs be in your right hand, and make them open their mouth and grip the surgeon's fingers between their hands, and press the tongue down to all the instrument, which is this form; and let it be made of silver or very fine tin as thin as knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue with all this tool, and see the pus-filled abscess? Take an onion and place it in the almond, and pull it up harder than you can; take nothing from the tissues with it, then scoop it out with your tool, as shown here; which looks like some strength. And both the head are set straight, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and made of metal inside or of silver:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool at hand, scoop it out with forceps, as shown here:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make the incisions on one side and the other; and when you have completed one of the almonds, complete the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sick with hot water, or hot and easy-to-swallow water, and if blood drainage occurs, gargle with hot water, or peelings of cooked cherry stones, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the saliva is completely drained; then complete the cure until it becomes well; and do not allow any new abscesses to form in the throat other than the two almonds, then proceed similarly as for the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, which is called the small abscess; and had I well nearly closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and died if she remained like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so much that it had caused to become blocked both openings of the nose for two days.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hurriedly performed the operation, inserting an awl into one of them, then pulled out the other limb with a large portion of the bow. Then, I made another cut on the other side near the nose, and I had the mouth open and pressed against the tongue; afterwards, I inserted the awl into these abscesses and cut away part, only releasing a little blood. And thus opened the windpipe in the woman, she began to drink water and later wine, and I did not stop cutting from that abscess for a long time; the abscess grew right back again, filling up my empty space until it was no longer just small; then I sewed her up and cauterized inside the throat: thus he remained without growing. And left those parts, only God made of him after me.
de l’uve	from the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the return of blood flows into the eye, and it is filled out and extended, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it's distended and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, and you see that the extraction of pus has calmed down, and it's subtle; you should take it. And the one that is round, assembled, and not long, and it's red or reddish or black; you should avoid making an incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, regarding its swelling and length, you should have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with a tool as we mentioned before; then insert the needle into the eye, pull it out slightly, and remove it using two tools that I mentioned earlier during the incision of the two almond-shaped areas.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not apply force beyond the natural boundary; because if you do so, you will harm the voice and speech. After incision, use what we have told about in the incisions of two kidneys, and treat until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is prone to fear when being treated, it's necessary that you apply something in their sense of pain for cautery.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of the cautery is by using hot iron.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And when the patient feels their health returning, then press the tongue with the tool that we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and use brisk water to do so, ensuring it is neither too thick nor too clear; and employ the movement of this instrument, as described here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place our head with a hair or where we put the medicine, like in the movements of a spoon, and place the tool across all the medicine on the bile; and let the patient remain stationary on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth towards the medicine inside, ensuring it doesn't descend into the throat, and the wound heals. Then keep your hand over the medicine and press it onto the bile for half an hour's worth of quantity until you see that the irritation and actions of the medicine are subsiding; and if you notice this, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the tool on all the cotton above wax, until the cotton dries on the bile. And repeat this process as needed until the cauterization is perfect, then leave it to dry, and wait for four or five days afterwards. If you need to restart with medicine cauterization, do so, and after the cauterization of inside the bile, clean up that which was inside the medicine using a buttered cloth; rinse with cold water, and continue gargling until fully recovered.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This remedy is safer than the incision, not just the cautery; if it is treated with fumigation using this method, take camomile and myrrh and wormwood and rue and mint and similar herbs, and gather them all or any of them into one pot, and pour water into it, and let it boil; and ensure the pot is well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot place one cooking utensil according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it applies to gold or arsenic, and in either case, place the tips of one's shoulders into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises from the uterus through the vagina, while the uterus is necrotic; after that, repeat often, until the uterus dries up. Make sure you don't do this at the beginning of pus expulsion, because many things happen in that process; and don't perform this method during the decline of pus expulsion.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a reed and place an eggshell in the mouth of the patient so that it is not too hot for the patient; because the eggshell does not cause steam to burden the mouth. This is a good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, open in the throat bone or spine of fish, without anything else; if it is thus that you should apply what you can see, press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you may observe movement; and that which does not open at all and remains in the throat, you should make the patient vomit until the substance leaves; by chance if this thing is expelled through vomiting; or if the substance swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a small piece of dry bread; and attach to the sponge a thread, then swallow it again; and when she comes up to the surface, if it rises, and then proceed to draw out. And if this thing does not come out from what we have said, take one of a cork instrument according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the tools be adjusted near the neck so it can more easily enter the throat, have the head raised high above; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, so nothing goes beyond or pushes the bone inward; adjust the tools as they apply pressure on what is being removed, because if this happens, if you push it down too far, or pull force equally along the entire tool until it's done.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the windpipe
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never use bleeding as medicine for the veins, as I have explained in division by medical treatment; and if this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient at noon, then press their tongue with the instrument I've told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see blood, direct it with all my small inch or with subtle pincers suitable for this task.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it's not worth that, take a hair comb and place it in the throat of the patient, then apply pressure at the end of the comb to cause friction. And do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you bathe the patient in water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water and let the patient drink it by mouth. Let them swallow it immediately without delay. Move their hand often; as soon as they sense the water, they will urinate.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if they do not urinate as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the tool I mentioned in the treatment of the eye; repeat this many times, for it will expel without causing harm.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is as follows: you take a pan where charcoal sticks are placed and it's covered with a screen pierced in the middle, and in that hole is put the end of the instrument. Then pour your fumigation, and the patient puts the tip of the stick into their mouth, close their mouth so no smoke escapes but goes until the nose; and now the nasal passage will start to breathe out, if it doesn't exhale, then restart the fumigation several times; and let the patient feel thirsty and consume salty things and such, and do not drink water; and then it's necessary for them to excrete forcefully through this process.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tool that treats the mucus, when you can see it, resembles curved tongs for moving things into the throat; and at the tip, it has a shape like a doctor's beak, and it also has a rasping edge, so whatever she takes cannot leave; now see this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The nature of pus evacuations is as follows, according to memory recalling from both sides in this book, and they vary in perforation and size. This can be done in two ways; one is in its natural form, based on what it holds moisture-wise.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for those who are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses on the neck are different from those in the base, and the abscesses on the inner thigh are different from those that come to joints, and each has its judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if it is abscesses one should not pierce until the bowel has died according to its development; and for some that need to be pierced as soon as they are ripe, and do not die according to their development, such as abscesses below joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from joints, if they are cooked internally for some time, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint might be corrupted, causing a constriction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For the abscess is located within the main limb, and if you delay the puncturing until it's dead, it will harm the main limb. Or if it's located at the base, if you pierce or do so when it's dead; it should not that you puncture an abscess without digestion being completed, except for when it is at the base, that it might seep fully through and be inside, leading to a fistula; and cannot heal properly in a large period of time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it should be known when the time is for perforating the abscess which has died according to its completion, and this is when the pain eases, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and from the movement and sharpness at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it should be done where the perforation stays higher above the abscess or below it depending on its location, and where it opens outwards; and make the perforation long through the body, and if the abscess is in hands or feet, joints and nerves and arteries, and all places where there are no wrinkles.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the fatty part of the body, it is necessary that you wait for the puncturing until digestion has been fully completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before this, then the body gets full of venom from within him and is filled with all kinds of dirt; and by chance it hardens the skin and the parts beneath.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are no abscesses pierced along the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you use small incisions, small blades; and for large incisions, large blades, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it's appropriate to use leather and coverings; when they have become as rough as cloth, and are flattened, then it is necessary to do so similarly to how one treats infants: and for those that split into three angles, and those whose treatment is like the leaf of bay, as abscesses from corners; and if there are such where you make a round cut, and other cuts and similar cutting treatments.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those without a chief, like superficial abscesses, it's necessary to pierce them completely. And when the abscess is large and has grown substantially, you should pierce it but do not drain all its contents in that moment; instead, extract some part of it. Then flatten the abscess until it reaches the other side, then leave no means of drainage immediately after that; do this process multiple times from large to small, until the pus is drained completely. Similarly, if the patient has weak strength or is pregnant, or small children, or elderly and decrepit individuals.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For when it tries thrice with the opening of the vein, that perhaps kills the patient, and you would not know.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be cautious of this chapter, and when you have opened your abscess, if the wound appears, observe that the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a plain cut, then use linen or thick cotton patches; and if it's a large abscess with many cavities, then stitch one patch in each so they press against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess including some skin tissue, and sewed it back together internally, then fill it with old cotton or dry linen strips without moisture, and bandage up to the third day; then set it, and apply ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there occurs an evacuation of blood in your operation, you should apply cold and gentle pressure, dampen the cloth, and place it on the wound, changing it repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, you should manage the operation and treatment carefully. Use the powders I mentioned in this book when handling them. If it's an insect bite or if there is pus under the skin, it is advisable to place damp cloths soaked in wine and oil on the wound. If it's swollen, and the part of the body affected by a boil is soft, it's appropriate to cover with damp cloths soaked in water and oil, or cool wine and oil for three days, as we have said; then remove the pustule and clean it properly until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in treatments of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here comes the chapter.
des soros	of the womb
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Cysts form on small abscesses, and they are treated in ways that involve bandages, similar to a jeweler working with glass, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that have moisture like fat or swellings; and there are others that are hard and stony to the tailor's touch, and there is no doubt that they affect arteries without causing opposition.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the tasks of tailoring involve using all kinds of tools that are called "introduction tools", from which this formation comes afterwards, containing something.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, do the incision over its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape without leaving any part of the skin containing that moisture. For as soon as nothing remains in it, it returns immediately. Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; otherwise, in water and vinegar, and apply to the wound, leave it until the next day; and those who are affected by nighttime rest will be healed.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And always reapply the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know it does not stay during the night; then dress the wound with ointment suitable for that, while it is still clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in not-too-much fat, cut it out according to this shape, along its long axis; and drain its contents from all sides, and burn everything around, and apply your entire treatment's healing force to where it lies; and if you treat it against my advice, do as I instructed afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And similarly treat if it's stony [hard], and cut and cure as I have instructed you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting on the stone-abscess and moisture, it is easier because they have little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these abscesses or head it has no moisture, and of these future abscesses that I saw or head from an old woman; and found the abscess as a soft stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if one had pierced it, they would have done so well to make incisions as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or around the head, if they come from children's heads and ear roots, the opening should be as long as possible depending on them, for the blood to exit; and treat them as they should.
des scrophules	regarding scrophula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times an abscess occurs at the neck, and around the glands, and under the collarbones, and nowhere else on the body or chest, and they are soft, and they stick together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scab is properly inside its shell, as with the nut and abscess on the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scabs are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In this kind that you see well formed in the pit, and resembles the color of the skin, it is silent from each part and is not close to the collarbone nor near the artery or vessel, and is not deep; then it is necessary for you to handle it above, and remove it from each part, and stretch the two lips around the artery if needed, as we have mentioned about abscesses on the head; and do it slowly, making sure you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and avoid any tearing or cutting too deeply that could cause the hand to escape and see too far ahead, so you do not remove more than what is necessary.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it doesn't allow you to open, place vitriol in the wound, or any powders that stop blood loss, and restrain the wound; and leave it as long as the abscess is calmed down, and the wound has softened, then begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the patient is healed, return to your work until you complete it; then listen to your judgment if there remain any small pustules, cut and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is large vein under the root of pustule, it's not right to cut out that pustule from its root. Instead, tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off on its own without harm; then cover the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire pustule, it is necessary for you to assemble the two edges of the wound, and stitch them now, then there should be no excess left due to the size of the pustule.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	And it is necessary for you to understand how to cut the root of it, and drain out the pus, and stitch it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those pustules that have excess, pierce them where they open naturally; and pierce them in the same way as previously described, hanging down, then apply ointments and similar things to it, so that if it gets corrupted by the pus; and when the wound is well cleaned, then the ointment treatment continues until the flesh grows back, until it becomes healthy.
de squinance	Regarding obliquity or deviation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and wrote about the surgery of cutting the throat; but I never saw anyone do this in our land, it's just recorded from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting eyes, it is necessary that the incision of the throat known as "epiglottis" be performed; and one should not attempt this procedure alone, because all the veins and the windpipe are in danger for those with pus-filled abscesses either in their mouth or in the throat or between the two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is within the lymph channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut through three or four small cuts across between the two circles, in the quantity of the cut opening into it, not within the cartilage; and this kind of cut is suitable for dividing the epiglottis so there is no flesh left, and the vessels are long enough to prevent bleeding.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are fearful, it is necessary for him to extend the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then cut through the keur until he reaches the cheneil; and avoid any blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut down to the syfac, as we have said; and this has been demonstrated by the section across the flow of the cheneil which jumps out through the broken side, and due to loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed during which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two sides of the wound neatly, and all along the seam without touching the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause healing flesh to form, until it becomes sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albanus states that one should not perform this until the entire throat is blocked, and the patient is deemed dead, and there is absence of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	So cut on the epiglottis because the body can't heal properly here, and it breathes through the wound, thus avoiding death; and according to the old doctors' command they left the wound open until the disease's malice passes, which does so in three days or four. And then they instructed to stitch up the wound and clean it, as long as it was being treated. And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I witnessed a maiden take the knife, and stabbed it into her throat, cutting part of the channels around the windpipe. And I was called to treat her, and found her as though dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.
