I discovered the wound, and found the blood issuing from it, and indeed, there was no major vein or artery that led there but rather the windpipe, and the veins flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurriedly treated the wound and healed her until she was cured; and there was nothing left to be done for the maiden except that her voice became rough, and she returned afterwards to her usual state. For this reason I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis, one should not have fear.
de la grosse gorge	In the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cysts called "glossocele" are referred to as large abscesses of a purple color, and are very common in women. They can occur in two ways: naturally or through accidents; natural ones do not have a cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And accidents occur in two ways: one resembles greasy matter coming from us, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from our arteries. And there's fear, so you shouldn't operate with fire except for those that are small; prove and seek all within: if you find it similar to what we produce grease, and it doesn't go towards any artery, then remove it as one would remove grease, and remove everything of its sheath; if there is nothing at all; search thoroughly and treat it accordingly until it's fully healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways there are, so I shall speak of all appearances; and it suits that I should state the full difference between us and issues.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is characterized by heat and fever lasting until the body's fluids have disappeared and decay has occurred; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the normal state, there is no fever, no pain, and contains its own sac, which is its own internal organ and is colored like the body's tissues, starting off somewhat like a cyst, and then grows larger; and shows up in two appearances, greasy or moist, and varies in color as I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of a new injury that you first try and inquire about all the tool which is called "the introducer", according to its form or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method for probing our wounds is that you should probe it as moist as you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers gradually until you know that the instruments have pierced the core, then do so according to the size of the abscess; then remove the pus, and be careful not to rupture it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs along it, regardless of its nature, whether it's cut like I said for other abscesses; and if after the incision no moisture comes out, know that it's greasy, then cut diagonally, take hold of it with pincers, lightly scrape each side and keep the coat where it lies. And if you can't remove it whole, then pull it piece by piece so that nothing remains attached.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, it comes back to the patient many times; and if only a little stays behind, without causing him pain, you fill the wound with corrosive powders, keep the wound clean, and place healing dressings over abscesses that are hot. You heal other treatments until he is whole again; and if the wound is large, stitch the two sides of the wound together, and treat the one that surrounds it in this way.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is larger than what is contrary or another thing that requires urgency, prepare the wound with vinegar and let it sit for two days or three days, until the wound heals from inside out. Then resume treating where you left off after removing the old material.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of instruments for internal drainage, and there are three ways: large, medium, and small. And among these there are three which are called 'albaret', and one that is called 'breb', and among them there are also three types: large, medium, and small to encircle abscesses; they resemble needles used to sew, made from citrine amber, iron or silver, yellow ones are preferred as they hold better than black beeswax for enclosing pus-filled areas. They come in three forms: large, medium, and small according to the width of the canals.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the trepan blades resemble that of a sheep, as you can see here: large, medium and small. There are also trepan blades with two horns in three ways; there are those with three horns and they too come in three types; some have two horns and others just one horn, all these also come in three forms. All these are needed in their proper place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these ones that we sharpen, and among such who cut only from one side, they burn the skin, for in this it is not cutting veins or nerves; and those intruders are answered with long needles in their hands, so that the patient does not notice during abscess opening; and there are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and none of them use any force but within the fatty area, like legs, arms, nipples, and joints, and similar parts; and every time a different small instrument is used, resembling surgeon's saws, according to this form, with which we stop bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed only once in its proper location among veins that are repaired and arteries, and never follows this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	None of the men's nipples swell up when they begin to become corrupted, until they seem like women's nipples; and remain swollen and puffy, and anyone who wishes to cure them should do so according to this form of this line .b. until .g..
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Trim the fat, then apply medicine to the wound to encourage flesh growth. Then join the two edges of the wound with stitches and continue treating until it heals. If the nipple tilts downwards due to its size as in women, cut into it from above making two similar incisions; one should hold onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line encompasses the smaller according to this shape, following this line .b.until reaching this line .g.; then trim the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, as well as anything necessary for treatment until it heals. If it has not healed or if the incision is not fully complete due to the discomfort of the patient or blood flow issues, fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment; leave it till it heals then remove the cotton and fat, then continue treating until completely healed.
des apostemes des asselles	removal of abscesses and boils
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from the armpits are methods of scrophula nodules or swellings, and if there are any containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to the line .g:.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus from within the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it for another day, then remove all the cotton and apply ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, cut it as we have said in cuts for scrofula sores, and if the wound is filled with pus, apply a cautery as we said previously.
de la routure de l’artere	Regarding the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is exposed, and if there are numerous abscesses, this also happens with the inflamed vein and abscess; and if one knows that it's due to an artery, then these abscesses should be long and deep; and when you feel resistance with your fingers, that means they're pressing strongly; and when it's due to a vein, pus is prominently appearing; this is foolishness to treat such abscesses, and similarly when there are other sores and swellings around the neck and in other parts of the body, and they are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the iron cure, and one should also avoid it for the head. In that which is swollen from an artery, cut through the skin as long as you can above; then proceed with surgery up to the oncines, and meticulously extract the artery from the tissues until it's fully exposed; then insert a needle under this area, and pierce it up to the other side, and firmly tie the artery with a double thread as I have taught you in extracting two arteries found in temples. Then pull out the body located between these two threads using an introducer tool, ensuring that no pus escapes from where it is, and free the abscess; then apply the ointment that suits this one until it heals completely. If the abscess is due to inflammation of a vein, you should dye your hand as much as possible with pus on the skin before you pull out the needle you hold in your hand, pierce it again, and ensure the double thread is secure; then tie up the abscess while cutting off all excess matter, leaving only that which is tied. Then apply a dressing soaked in wine and oil until it heals completely, and continue with bandages and ointment applications until it fully heals.
des apostemes des ners	removal of abscesses or nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like an abscess can form in the artery and vein, an abscess may develop in nerves when they are injured or due to excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this often happens to shoulders and elbows and in all places where joints are found, it is the case of abscesses, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and can be in many positions without pain; and when it is squeezed forcibly, the patients feel great pain and does not match well with the body but just under the skin; and moves very much from all directions, neither forward nor backward, neither up nor down, and what is jointed cannot properly cover with iron: by chance there would be a contraction; and that which is on head or forehead makes the skin hollow.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and you have forceps, apply them at its base; and if it's large, hold it by the wrist, and scrape it off, then expose the bone, stitch up the wound in place, and treat until it heals completely.
des grosses boces pendans	And for large tumors, they are suspended
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	No instance occurs within the belly or elsewhere in this fashion, and it is a disease given the name "fungus" by its appearance. It has a fine root and big seeds; there are also small ones of various sizes. I knew someone who had two bellies that appeared more like fungus than anything else, and there was no difference between them. They were white in color, with thin roots, and were cut open, and they corroded due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I measured and found that in the first one it weighed eighteen ounces, and in the other six. The organs are as follows: when you look during incision, if you notice that the tissues are moist, their color is white and wet with a fine root; if you touch the spume area widely, then apply the fire cautery to them.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in surgery there are often many times too large hemorrhages and if you do not stop them, then quickly use a cautery; and when you see the patient scared and fearful at the metal incision from the iron, then take a well-made catgut thread and tie it around as we said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten, and continue pulling on the catgut until it covers the metal tool without any struggle; and if the roots are large, get them scared by the stomach's pull itself but you can tie only half properly first, then cauterize so they don't reappear; then treat the wound and make sure not to tie up a slippery thread of dirty color and poor feeling and milk smell.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess that has opened up, and I will come to the treatment of gangrene next.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the elbow bone twists
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	When it appears like a boil comes from the wound cautery or tear in the intestine, and this is on the belly and there are some boils elsewhere, as happens in other wounds, or bleeding which comes from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned beforehand, or due to windiness; and if this is by the tear of the intestine and through the exit of the pus, then its color resembles that of blood, and it has little feeling with little pain, and opens up through different exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it's due to the opening of the intestine, then it becomes more varied, and when one presses it with their fingers it comes back and then returns, and by chance it might tighten up and enlarge much at the entrance of the bath and through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it's due to moisture, it's a simple matter, and opens well when you press on it with your hand, without restraining it; and if it's due to blood, it will open through these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and appear following a quantity; and if it's due to wind, it stings at touch, and the symptoms are that you observe whether its appearance is due to the blood of an artery, or a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you allow the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear about it, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if its appearance is due to the intestine or the bladder, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to bleed their body, and have it stretched completely straight, then cut all around the belly; then order them to treat with vinegar between your hands, then go into the area where you indicated on the body, and remove half of the abscess above the largest part of the belly button; then tie that half of the abscess onto a strong thread or thick silk string firmly, and secure it tightly; then stretch out the other half of the abscess over this bandage, and bend your index finger, and pull on the intestine; if you find it caught in the bandage, untie it, and pull the intestine to the outside of the belly; and if you find the bladder, take hold of its tip, and remove any excess; and if the artery or vein goes against you, or goes well into it, then return to your work and take two needles, and tie two strands of thread onto it, and place those two needles in cross where you pierced previously; then pull on the abscess in four places through the needles, and if you see that it is ready, remove the needles, and let the body heal itself, and remove any dead flesh by itself; or you cut it when it has become tender and ready, then treat as we have said; and drain out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the body according to what needs to be done, and shave off the abscess.
dou chancre	towards the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the appearances of gangrene and how to treat them with medicines, and how to avoid iron treatment. Let us say that gangrene grows in the armpit, and great caution is needed when treating it. The old ones said that if gangrene appears where you can scrape it off, such as on the nipples, in cooking areas, and similar body parts, then you should remove all of it at the beginning; and when it becomes large and old, one should not approach it at all because I have never known anyone to heal from it. Nobody has ever healed under my care before.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez. de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément. Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones which are indwelling in the bladder occur more often among children, and this is a sign that the infection jumps from the bladder akin to an infection that manifests through subtlety; they open the urethra, and rub the patient's penis, and he urinates many times, and then it gets caught. And at these jumps of the stone, its base can be found; and for several months, children's healing is light until they reach four years old, it causes much discomfort in the elderly, and occurs in middle age, to those who are between adulthood and old age; and the treatment for those with large stones is lighter than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient through sweating, in order to draw out all the pus from within their intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And it impedes every time when one seeks to cut into the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take hold of the patient with their hands, and pull them down backwards, so that the stone descends to the bladder's level and emerges nowhere above him; then have them sit between your hands, with their arms under their thighs, making sure that the bladder is fully lowered downwards; next, search for it internally; if you feel the stone in the space, now hurry to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier. And make the division between what is in between the hips and the foundation, not mid way but at the edge of the left snowbank; and be straight upon the stone, and your hands either to the ground or the foundation, and be the size deep through such that it is wide outside and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; by chance if presses the hand which is on the foundation, make it jump out easily with no effort; and know there are parts of rock where there are angles and edges: if it gets stuck coming out; and if at part below, resembling a walnut, and round, where its outlet is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And in the places where there are angles and edges, make the hole larger; if it does not jump out, you must press with the tongs that are as sharp as a file to force the stone so that it does not escape. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if she is very large, then it must be opened, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: or he dies, or his urine starts coming out immediately as soon as his legs cannot join; but still strive to drain or remove it with forceps until you can extract it piece by piece. And when you loosen it, make sure to sit upright from the oil and water well, then bathe with dyacina ointment and basil ointment until they are healed.

And if abscesses become infected in the wound and blood clots form in the bladder, and then urine retention occurs as it is known to do, force your way into the wound then extract that blood, because if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and ruin it; then raise the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help him in every way you can until he heals; and when you treat him always, tie his two legs together, and apply medicines to the neck.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it's located where the penis leads, and stuck inside, causing inability to urinate; if this is what you treat as I described, you should repeatedly cut it several times, considering the loss due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already gained this experience.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron according to this shape and have it pierced at three corners in one point:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the penis near the stone so that it doesn't come back into the bladder; then pull out the needle gently in the penis until it reaches the stone; and turn the needle with your hand in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; if the urine comes suddenly, then press your hand on what is stuck inside the stone which is within the penis.

de la piere des femmes	From the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stone is found in women, and if it occurs once, the treatment is difficult, and is prohibited for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to expose herself even when she is pure.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. And the third method is that by chance it may not be possible to find a woman well versed in this art of hands; and the fourth method is that the stone of the woman is more pronounced than the stone of man, so one must make deeper cuts, there's great fear involved. And if necessity calls for such actions, then you should seek out someone who knows well and take their advice on where to cut within her body. If you can't find this person, don't hesitate to consult a subtle surgeon; and present a skilled midwife in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, command her to do as you instruct regarding the examination of the stone; and look very closely if that woman is a virgin: thus she must press her index finger against or on the stone; and when she finds it, restrain her with this index finger, and advise her to press her index finger onto or in the diseased area, and press her left hand firmly upon her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder until underneath; until she reaches the root of the thigh; then cut into the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the knee joint, where they appear, and feel the bone in that area; and do not move your hand above the bone or below, and make a small incision first; then push out the kidney with pressure at this size; as long as you can feel the bone increase the wound until the bone can come out forcefully, and know that many types of stones are: namely, small and large and hard and smooth, long and round, and those that have furrows.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you understand the symptoms to know its outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it doesn't frighten him, then apply vitriol to the wound and hold it for an hour until the fear subsides; then return to your work until the stone is out, and have the tools I told you about in removing stones to assist you in your task. And if it doesn't frighten him, but what was cut off is from the artery, then apply powder to the wound and tighten with threads and binders, and do not repeat this again, and leave the stone alone without pulling it out, for fear that he might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of blood has been calmed and your limbs are recovered, return to your task until the stone becomes soft.
de hernie carnouse	of fatty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery hernia is nothing else but a gathering of moisture or white yolk, which is found in the area around the kidneys, contained within the egg; and it's called "yolk", and one cannot properly find it on the surface of the egg if one thinks it's another egg; and this is the skin under the kidney containing the white yolk that we have mentioned; and this doesn't have any hole.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of such a watery hernia is due to weakness that affects the kidneys, and this spreads that substance.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it come from percussion on the kidneys, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a declining color to jaundice, or it's without redness, or black, or aqueous white. And this happens more; and these are signs to recognize this assembly. For if it is pure white as we have said, then pus will be present, lasting as long as the kidney's figure is an egg, and doesn't open the kidneys, because there is moisture everywhere inside.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if he has moisture in the proper tissue, then there will be pus with part of an egg, and because of this we think it's another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the kidney and the pure white, you'll feel it well; therefore when you know the color of the moisture, test everything inside carefully, as described here.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this then, who comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside him.

de l’aposteme des coions	regarding the pus of the ears
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the part of this branch there is fear for multiple arrangements, so I believe movement would be better if one were to leave it; and I will tell you about the operation and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, it is known that many abscesses can occur on the body or limbs; and this happens due to various reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know about superfluous acidity and mucus which spreads among the joints or due to percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no pain, it's a diseased abscess; and occasionally there's a pungent and stone-filled pus, with a reddish color, and it never comes from a vein or inflates a wound.

Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	So do not hasten to pierce it at once, but wait until the pain is relieved; and then have the patient sit on the stool, with two small stools placed under his elbows as he leans forward, supporting himself against his back and gathering his legs towards the parts below the leg; and let his knees spread out, place his arms under his thighs, and bind them firmly together with a good bandage; then direct him to breathe towards his right side, guiding the tool used for the operation of the boil from its mouth, which comes afterwards in this form; it is necessary that when you see this tool being guided, you set about measuring the depth of the boil, so that what enters through the instrument does not go any further than it should and cause pain to the patient; and if the instruments are too large, cover the depth of the boil with cloths, so that the tools do not bother the patient; it is necessary that he place the funnel of the tool above him and cut the tool.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement. de l’enfantement	Regarding childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The profession starts with knowing the form of natural birth, and indeed recognizes these signs: when you see a woman laboring intensely to deliver and longs to smell something fragrant, then the baby will soon make an appearance. This indicates that the birth is proceeding naturally, from her head, and secondarily through him; when you observe these signs, lightly press her abdomen so the baby can come out promptly. For when it descends from its head, it brings along the afterbirth, which is cleansed of its excesses by good postnatal care; anything else that occurs otherwise does not happen naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier. de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the birth of the child above its feet

Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhage is from the root or base of an abscess, or from a deep lesion, and if it is as subtle as for an infant; and this is the form of a subtle cyst under which the skin is constrained:
des plaies	from wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have spoken about the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will discuss treatments for hands and medicine according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I state that wounds are diverse depending on how they were made, and where the wounds are located, and why they were caused.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that result in injuries are through the breaking of bones, and cuts from a sword or dagger, or lance or staff, or similar objects; or those done according to the parts of the body, such as an injury at the neck, or on the head, or stomach, or belly, or liver, and similar organs; and I will tell you how each wound is treated, beginning with simple wounds of the head, for this knowledge will come up in my chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I state that when a simple wound occurs or bone is damaged, and the bone isn't broken, you must be cautious whether it's due to stone or similar things, and even if the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly about pus formation: if you perform immediate surgery on the cephalic region precisely when there is little blood from the wound, and then heal in opposition to the affected part; let the patient replete with wine and consume large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they do not want to undergo surgery, reduce their meat intake, and do not drink wine or eat large meats; instead place on the wound, if pus is present, moist cotton soaked in rose oil or in a收敛ive wine; and if there is no pus present, apply on the fresh wound as long as it has all its blood without being disturbed by air, then use powder which I will explain shortly; and if it has been disturbed, apply some remedies until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like from a sword cut and similar injuries, and the lips cannot be stitched together by tents, then stitch them together, as I will explain for wounds of the abdomen, in stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound exposes the bone, and might, and can only hold for a bit, if you can manage; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, like cooked tests and wheat, as well as cooked chickens, and similar items.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or discover rotting skin, and it doesn't reach the bone, then remove the rot completely, and drain pus, then treat; and if there is an artery inside the wound or vein, without a cut, and it cannot be stopped with medicines, then tie the artery, and if you notice dislocation, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, their treatment is light: and you should apply this powder which will stick together in such a way that when the fire touches it, it heals.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way to make the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and finely ground it all; then spread this over the wound and press it firmly until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then tie it properly and leave it without loosening it if it doesn't swell; because you don't remove the medicine until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Only this is done with salt alone, when one doesn't have the incense or the blood of the dragon, but only when the art has healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has healed the wound, indeed in this state, he should not apply this powder at all; but instead use some well-prepared ointments, or oats flour mixed with water and honey until it no longer oozes. Then continue other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone breakage comes with the wound and it is small, then try using subtle needles; and I will tell you about bone fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound at the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and those at the head, but if a nerve in the neck or an artery has been cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's in the nose, if there is no other tool but to let the cure alone, and not put anything restraining on it, as it harms the nose and makes them recede; and do not put anything cold on the wound, as the substance of the nose is cold, and its continuous use involves the head which is the highest member; but apply the medicine underneath, such as rose water mixed with mild oil, and cooked lettuce rinsed in gentle water, and other earthy minerals according to this method, and wet bandages.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, bind it with strips and then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deeply cut and filled with blood, then pierce them or lower down. And if an artery is severed, and bleeding occurs, then open it up, clean it out, and cauterize; and if the spine of the throat, or ribs, and the passageway is cut, guard where the meat goes, so that when you set the rib on top of the neck bone, don't touch the throat but place it according to its natural shape; and then adjust the setting, leaving it for a few days. Then treat with dried ointments until it heals; and if there appears to be an impact in the bone, seek treatment for that; and if pieces of bone are present, remove them all you can, and those that cannot be reached, let them stay until the wound becomes healed and drained, then dry out its source. And if the wound is fresh, apply powder as I have said on top of the powder.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as instructed in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from lance or knife wounds
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a lance or knife wound and the injury is deep, then look at how the wound is healing: if there are signs of wind escaping from the body instead of the patient's blood alone: this means that the injury is fatal; and if it isn't deep and the whole area still has fresh blood, then don't apply any powder or bind it until the first hour passes. Let the blood drain naturally outwards rather than stopping completely, allowing the heart to take over and ensure the health of the patient. But instead use an attracting ointment and bind it twice a day; if you have no ointment, put old cotton into the wound for soaking up moisture. Make the patient rest on the wound for three days or four, or more if necessary. If there are no signs of spasms or trembling from the heart, then the injury is saved when you see improvements in healing conditions and can ascertain that the injury has been resolved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat with various remedies and other treatments until it heals; and if it does not heal or work properly, know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and it's simple or worse, at the front; for large wounds use stitches; and for small ones, powder. If the wound goes through bones and breaks them, and if there are pieces of bone, consider how to treat the wound along with the foreign objects inside; and if they are exposed, leave the wound to fester until they can be removed; and if they aren't exposed, allow the wound to heal naturally, facilitating extraction procedures for others. For wounds on other body parts, make judgments accordingly as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The operations on the belly are large, medium and small; from a major wound, an intestine or pieces of intestines may be cut out due to the insertion of objects; sewing is more complicated, and in no case is it worse than the smaller wounds compared to larger ones because if we try to reinsert them too soon after surgery, they might not fit properly; as intestines swell when they feel cold, making reinsertion difficult, which means that smaller wounds are better off. You should know that the rupture of the belly can happen in four ways: the common two types of stitches occur during a belly operation, and the other stitches for other body parts are also used but with operations on the belly; however, they are more precise when dealing with belly stitches, and I will explain each one separately.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and no part of the intestines is involved, and if there are only minor injuries requiring treatment, this can be done through one of two methods: either because of the size of the wound as we've explained, or due to the intestines being swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm him in this manner: soak an sponge or a cloth with water only, or cook them in boiling water with quina and thyme and spices, and expose the intestines until they become hot; and after doing this several times, let him cool off to help reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you notice the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with water or broth from cooked vegetables, for this helps in allowing food to pass through easily; and if it doesn't enter, cut a little bit more of the wound using the tools used for cutting stitches; and the first cure is cooling off, followed by surgery, which should only be done when there's significant need; and these are the tools used for cutting: you cut inside along the curve and not outside, and then follow this form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have jumped out, if you can, put them back according to their natural shape in their proper place, for this suits a return.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is broad, and it's in the abdominal region, it should be that you make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head. And if it's in the abdominal area, then place their head and bottom above the abdominal parts, and similarly, when the belly wound is in one of the two areas, put your understanding so that the part that has been cut off is higher than the other; and thus you should follow what I'm saying about large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you are provided with, then take the surgical tools that cut completely through the wound with your hand, and stitch together the edges; this is the common way of sewing, and it involves using one or more needles according to the size of the wound. Leave a space from the edge of the wound about an inch, then insert a needle at any point where you think the thread will hold well, followed by thick strong thread; and pierce both parts through the skin with both ends of the sewing tool which is inside the skin, until it pierces that part, then gather both ends of the sewing tool together into three. Then sew through the skin twice, leaving about half an inch from each stitch, then insert another needle; and tie this thread as you did for the first needle, without ceasing to do so based on your need of needles until all the wound is secured; use needles that are neither too fine nor too thick, because very thin needles cut all the flesh, while overly thick ones don't fit well: thus they should be medium-sized; and don't make the stitches too deep into the flesh and skin, as this will cause damage during healing. Afterward, tie off the ends of the needles so that they don't irritate the patient at night, and place cloths or bandages over the needle parts to hold them down while letting the wound heal; and let this sewing process continue until the wound is joined; and this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as you join both skin ends and both flesh ends together into one needle where there's a medium strong thread; when you've pierced these four parts together, pull the needle back to where you started, in the manner that you sew clothes. Leave space between each stitch about an inch wide; this stitching heals the person, and I once stitched a wound of someone who was cut by a knife, which was over one palm long, and had intestines nearly two palms thick, and was in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back his intestines until it had been 24 hours since its removal, and the wound was sown up till 15 days later, and I treated him, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And when they had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in an area where none could be found, nor any medicine. Instead, I placed two layers of old cloth on the wound each day, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and pierce from the outer side until it reaches inside; when it has pierced through the skin straight in and out, then place the tip at the siphon or where you have pierced the skin with the needle, and make another hole on the inner side until it reaches the outer side again. And the principle of this stitching is that you sew as a mole does with its fur, leaving an opening on one side and picking it up from the other, until the entire suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, as Galen properly stated, is such that none do it, who join the two parts together naturally, and apply one edge to the other edge like this: pierce with a needle or an edge near the thread, just pierce the left part only, and leave the two edges of the thread. Then turn the needle and make it pierce from below forward until into these parts as far as the two edges of the thread; then pierce both from below forward until into these parts in two other threads that are at the opposite side. And this is the way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and none testify it, that one should stitch the abdomen with two needles or threads in each; and one should pierce one needle from one side and the other from another, like those who sew joints. Know that when the rupture is within the abdomen, the stitching is worse than among their others' of the stomachs.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments concerning the wound are such as those for other wounds: and thus when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, just like you have let the heat of it go out, then return the intestine and the lip; afterwards put on the stimulating powder on meat.
