Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drained, one can only say until completion: so then it becomes necessary for you to bind the head above and below with a very tight strong rope, then cut upwards and drain forcefully, and if blood is not found, should then cauterize with fire until it stops; and all major damages that it causes, are when they run into the eye, as we have said; and should you see it approaching or nearly to the eye, should then hold firmly underneath him with the eyelid form, cut upwards, and drain forcefully; it is necessary to use the aid of purification through body fluids of medicinal solvents for the ailments caused by humors, and watch out for meat spoilage resulting from fermentation.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from winds.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it's a pain that comes to any limbs, and then moves from one limb to another; I've seen the case as I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to attend a sick woman and found her arms exposed. I noticed a small swelling in the arm vein; shortly after, I saw it rise as if a worm was entering the shoulder, faster than any other object, like quicksilver being poured from one hand to another; the pain left that hand and lodged itself in the shoulder. Then soon afterwards, it spread throughout her body until it reached the other arm; she then told me that the pain was looping within her body, just as I had observed.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much how she moved from limb to limb in this way, for I had never seen this disease carried out like this before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	To conclude, I have wished for many times that the pain could move from one place to another, but it was not done like this before what I observed in her. And I thought that this happened because of the woman's dry body and exposed veins, as well as due to this constrained wind; yet they do not appear thus according to this reason among those who are healthy and have moist bodies with covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see the treatment for this illness, and the patients feel that pain, if it opens up as we have said, then press on it quickly both above and below, and then apply pressure until that constraining wind strength escapes from the place; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it at your ears, treat those who debout the winds, like stinking pills, serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary according to their shape and the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of arrows is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed, and soldered; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those where pieces exist. And the way these arrows exit does not follow any particular pattern: some go out at the main body parts like the head, brain, heart, liver, stomach, intestines, bladder, and other primary organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it comes to any part of the body, and the signs of death which I will tell you later, they appear: so it is necessary that you prepare for the extraction of this arrow, because death follows in various dispositions; and when that bad sign does not appear and the arrow has not been fully extracted, then remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign for the brain when the arrow has penetrated and pierced the bone, there is bleeding from a faucet that's under the head, and if blindness, deafness, inversion of vision, red eyes, inflammation and red tongue, seizures, confusion in understanding, vomiting of bile; and perhaps loss of strength through nostrils or ears; and sometimes loss of speech and voice; and pus appearing like a boil at the wound; and also as burned flesh. And if these signs appear, then take action on treatment, extract the arrow if it's not yet done.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it leaves or pierces the heart is that it's close to the left breast, and feels like it might be stuck in something solid, not empty; and sometimes the arrow remains silent just like the pulse, with black blood and cold sweat coming out, and a chill sensation: knowing this without doubt means death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never leaves is that there's no foam spill from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's skin changes color, and they sigh loudly with a chill in their breath.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow closes in the thigh's covering, it affects the small bones; and there is great pain and great distress, with sighing; and they move all their limbs from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow penetrates or touches the stomach, by chance it leaps out of the wound without digesting any substance.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow penetrates or touches the belly, and leaps out without passing through any intestines, then there is no hope for treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder and urine flows out and escapes, causing severe pain to the patient: you must know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other body parts, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and shoulder blade and elbow and collarbone and ribs and back muscles, and thighs, and similar limbs are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the muscle or artery and it's not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because when you do something else.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one house where an arrow hit him in the thigh at the root of his leg: I tried it and pulled it out from another side through the fat behind the ear, causing no intense pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And pulled out an arrow that had hit him in the fat around the eye, near the paper skin behind it. The arrow was stuck, and only reached half way towards the shaft, measuring as large as a Turkish bow's length without any of it visible; the game was done quickly, and no ill accidents occurred to the player.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And try to extract an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and there was an Arabic arrow in his ear: I pulled at the arrows, made them thinner as I pulled, and saved the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And try to extract an arrow from the body, which was stuck in either his chest or abdomen, and I thought he would die; and then after thirty days had passed, if his condition did not change, I cut into the arrow, pulled it out, and there were no adverse incidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you find a person with an arrow that has fallen on or behind them, and the wound is sealed up; and the arrow stays inside, and does not alter its natural disposition, nor finds any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And to another man, who was hit in the face with an arrow and had the wound stitched up; and he suffered great pain ever since; and many others were similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow hit the home of the princes' king, who was in the midst of their battle zone, and it leaned slightly to the right side; and the arrow was fully embedded. I was called for the treatment after it had been embedded for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound significantly constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to remove it with great subtlety, and did not feel it; and there was pain and discomfort spreading across his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a therapeutic plaster and digestive aid on him because his ears did not swell; and it appeared that there was the arrow in his ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the healing poultice for days, and quickly resolved the wound, then let the patient suffer long henceforth, until they felt the arrow inside their nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed corrosive blood-purifying medicine on the wound for days until it opened, then tried it out and felt the tip of the arrow moving towards its socket. Then I aligned the opening of the wound with that medicine, up to when the head of the arrow became clearly visible; and pressed through well for about four months, afterwards stretching the wound so I could grip the clamps from both sides and not be able to pull it out; then did not stop refining and inventing ways with tools until one day I grasped the arrow in properly made clamps, according to what its shape will look like by the end of this chapter's treatment, when I pulled it and left the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it thusly, and once the wound has been sewn up, and the patient fully healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so please apply your skill to what I am not saying, because books cannot cover everything; but wise masters compare well on a few small matters and on what is current or lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in dealing with the events that occur in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I state that arrows penetrate the limbs at their entry points for two ways: either through the upper part where they enter or from another direction; and if it is through the side where they entered, then the arrow goes into the flesh, and there has been no penetration so far.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump now, let it grow until the chariness is thoroughly treated internally and relieved; similarly if it's implanted in bone, and can't emerge, leave it like that for some days, and remove it each day; then it will jump. If it doesn't jump, drill through all the way inside with a very fine tool as long as the lungs are expanded internally, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if an arrow is implanted in the bone of the head and extends up to one of the lungs within the brain, or encounters any of the incidents I've described clearly for the patient: do not remove it immediately, but let it grow until it is even after some days, because should the arrow reach this far, it's a death sentence.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only implanted in the bone and does not extend to the sinus, and remains with no adverse incident for any days, then proceed with the extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is so deeply embedded and cannot come out, then administer warm baths internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals properly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned to its original position within the body so that you can't see it, then seek it with all your senses; and if you feel it, try to pull it out with any suitable tool; and if you cannot due to the wound's constriction or the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves or veins involved, then cut as large an area as possible; and when you can pull the arrow out, remove any flesh stuck in two parts from both sides that moves along with it, and then break or bend the ears on the arrow while trying to pull it out; make sure not to break the arrow, so you could pull it out more tightly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't do it all at once, if until the middle of your arm is still sore, then try again, because the extraction will be easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding from the wound causes you to contradict our previous advice about treatment in this chapter, then follow what we have said regarding care; and be cautious of cutting near nerves or arteries, and do it gently according to your ability to pull out the arrow without risk, whether quickly or cautiously, firmly or gently; and treat the patient according to their original condition when they were hit by the arrow, for this is their greatest assistance, and if you cannot do so, then place them in a position indicated by the sign that shows them.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another side, where it opens some part of the body or swells the skin visibly in place: cut up there, as long as the forceps can take hold, and then press: if jumping occurs now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is caught in the bone, twist your hand around it until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, let her stay in there and then continue the extraction as long as she lets go; and if the arrow is inside her, hold it with all the shaft; and if it is a bullet, when you see how to administer pressure, if you give direction of administration, if you offer the tool with the point entering first, so that the tip of the arrow enters into the opening of the tool; and then force her, and if she shoots out, then use the tool with the point entering last in order to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow touches it, you should take all of the flesh around where I come in, if possible, then treat the wound according to what is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow hits or pierces somewhere in the leg, belly, bladder, or side, and it is close to vital organs, you should cover up there, if possible; and beware not to cover the vein and the nerve, then remove it, and then stitch up the wound when necessary; and treat until she/he heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used for arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And in terms of size they are as follows: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird, meant to pierce at the tip of the arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape for gripping and pulling like tongs is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	from the veins of common horns
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins from which we drain are thirty-one, of which there is or head sixteen. This means: Two batans located after the ears, which are called "two 'herbech'"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples visible; and two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the tip of the nose; and two jugulars located on the neck; and two veins that are above the lips of the mouth, these are the veins called 'augeherich'; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly treated are V in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it's at the left rib, and they call it among laymen "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faster", and it's made up of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it among laymen "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is either at the left or right rib, and they call it among laymen "vein of the belly", and it's above the clavicle, and it's the one that gets treated, which opens up clearly on the belly.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The arm vein is the vein that's between the thumb and the ring finger, and it exists in two parts; and in the leg and where the foot is, there are three veins: one of which is beneath the bend of the ankle at the left rib, and the second is sophene which is at the ankle at the right rib; and the vein that's called "ness", which is in the ankle on the other rib; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.

Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses. Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the heated suction cup applied is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And the size of this tool is two and a half palm lengths across, it has its edge located at about halfway along its center like piercing an eye, similar to sticking a needle in, so as not to harm the patient when placing it on limb; there is also a middle part that is a crosswise piece from spider or iron, for attaching a candle, and they come in large sizes and small ones according to different illnesses and the conditions of those who use them; because children's suckers are different than those for adults, and for skinny people compared to fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And when to apply this suction cup to the limb: take the candle wick or the thread and insert it through the hole in the suction cup which is located at the center part, ensuring that light is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, put your fingers on the part we just mentioned, such that if needed, when the vapor goes out and removes the suction cup; and take the thread as before, repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup then, which is administered in the illness of pleurisy, there should not be any length or defect at all, and it should only be applied when it is full of water, and placed solely on the body member; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without doubt they are administered only in limbs where one cannot place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and on their dry skin, like elbows or knees, and other similar conditions; and the quality of their use is that when you find suckers that are in sweet waters without pollution, you take them; and you place a nut in sweet water until they become accustomed, without having anything in their guts; and then cleanse with bloodletting and suction cups, then rub the body part until it turns red, and place them on the suckers; and when they are full, and start to withdraw, if there is a part where one can place a suction cup, you place it, because this works quite well afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the limb in cold water, quite well, then heat it; and if the limb is not fully healed after a while, apply damp linen cloth dipped in cold water, until the skin becomes moistened; and if there are many blisters, apply powdered glass or vinegar, until they dry out; or you put half of peeled beans on the limb and leave them until they steam up inside it, which will stop bleeding now; and if you need more, take other blisters.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the blisters do not form again, rub the limb with fresh blood or stick an awl in it until a blister forms. Then leave them there, and as soon as they start smelling of blood, they will dry out; and when you see that they are discharging, sprinkle a little aloes and powdered flour over them or ash, which will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know that the young man, among these chapters, he finds nothing as such in the old books or letters; and because of this reason, the knowledge was taken away from our land, for I never found anyone good; and I know nothing myself, having studied through the knowledge of old books which I have spent so much time on, and through experiments, and according to my life's habituation; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the tools used, as done in the two chapters before these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it is necessary that we outline or introduce the main points of this book in its preface and chapters where the senses engage understanding, and remain truthful, so that those who have experienced it may know and learn this noble craft, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fractures or dislocations or twists or swelling occur in any part of the body, you must quickly cleanse the patient from one side to the other without any delay. If something is missing on either side, such as weakness, children, elderly people; or if the wound is too tight, or too cold; and if it contains cold juices, meaning cool joints and bile, and not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill up too much with meat that fills veins of blood until you are certain there's no pus formation in heat, nor spreading of matter into the limb; let the patient recover as per their initial commandment until they have used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you consume meats which cause heavy digestion or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and leeks, and kidneys, and pies, and beef spleens, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar items.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this kind of digestion causes motion and more quickly the breaking (or disruption) is resolved.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that a broken bone in old or decrepit people can't be repaired or joined properly according to its nature due to the drying of the limbs, nor for those that are too tender like small children's bones; but in your care, set the broken bone back with the larger tendons that come forth and unite the limb together, as long as it holds firm as before; and don't leave off his work entirely, for this requires nourishment from large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	Know that fractures occur in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot, or leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go to the arm, and others when sharpening, such as sawing through a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And in case of breakage with wound, and breakage resulting from a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in every way has its tool and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings to his mind; and he recognizes the breaking of the bone by the twisting of his fingers, and it opens well through them, and is pressed by hand; and when there is no twist or rubbing on his finger, and the patient does not feel much pain, if there is no breakage; but he may have a twist, or crack, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move it by hand, but apply the following remedies, and then gently correct it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that when the break occurred in motion, and those two parts were separated, they now need to be brought back to being equal, just as abscesses would heal; and if abscesses are left bleeding, you should not allow them for any day until the inflammation from them subsides; then set it level at its proper place that you can move lightly and wisely. Know that restoring this is easier than restoring those with pieces. Then hold it tight, as described later on.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bones have pieces broken, and they are divided into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or by your hand if it's a small limb, or in case of two tendons, or one tendon and by your hand; place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are freed, you remove all additions from their places at the part that moves as you can, and be careful not to cause any injury or pain to the patient with your work; adjust both ends of the bones properly according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if you think it is not quite right: do it beautifully in position, don't pull too much, and apply pressure as those who bring about discharge through a wound and muscle contraction do to the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limbs are in place, do well to restrain the patient so they don't move them, whether awake or asleep, turning over or in any other way; and make sure that the limb is securely set so it doesn't feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And when they do not feel any pain, it is not properly in place, and you should arrange them so that they do not feel any pain at all; and take care to put them back straightly, so that no twist occurs when they are restored; and the quality of the broken limb follows as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are various in size and degree, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	And for small limbs, such as arms and legs and alike: it is necessary to envelop them with soft and fine linen cloths; and for those that are large, such as thighs and calves: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and firm bandage, because the wider bands embrace all of the larger limb, and restrict it equally from all sides, so that there is no unevenness; then tie the bandages loosely around in three or four rounds according to the limb, and press your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the breakage point and apply less pressure, so that the breakage can move away a little bit; and soften the bandage gradually until you reach most of the healthy part, then repeat with another bandage, and tie them together tightly around the broken limb; then return to the area below the breakage point, and apply moderate pressure, neither too hard nor too soft, as we said in the previous section; then place linen or cloth bands between the tied bandages until they are all even, then secure everything above the bicephalic part with a bandage, and then place your well-made tacks accordingly, if there is no pus or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, you should place something soothing for the abscess above it and that reduces the swelling. Allow this state to continue for a few days; then begin treating your stars with these tools which are half the width of a thick reed, or parts of a staff used for making arrows, or palms' leaves, and treat them according to this form:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the stars you place over the dislocation are slightly larger and wider than the others; they should also be as long as required for the size or scale of the limb. Then apply them to the stars in the same manner as at the first application, then tie on an additional thread above them like you did before with the dislocation. The threads must become tighter now, and later less so. And it is necessary that the thread be of medium thickness; neither too thin nor too thick, made from soft linen. For if the thread is too thick, as in operations where they tie on cords made of twisted linen during their applications, this is a great mistake, because the application cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not have less than half an inch between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patients are injured by the rings after tightening them on their healthy parts, then put linen or woolen bandages over them, so they don't blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is swollen and the joints are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to strain all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to use iron balls after seven or eight days or more depending on the condition of pus appearing; and here is how the old plastering method restores fractures, dislocations, and twists: and you take flour that stands at mill walls, mix it with plenty of eggs, and make this concoction neither too thin nor too thick. Use this mixture properly and it is a common way to restore fracture with several variations, and similarly for women and small children, because it is not excessively hot or cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering for restoring fractures and dislocations and twists: take three parts of each of these ingredients - garlic, dill, rue, and asafetida - mixed with three times the weight in powdered gum arabic and myrrh; add five parts aloes. Grind all together into a fine powder and mix it with plenty of egg; if the mixture is warm, use this plaster, for it has a good composition and rapidly heals broken bones, and it is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plastering method for twists: take mugwort and valerian root, each in IX grams; myrrh and aloes, each in IX grams; stonewort in VI grams; Armenian balm in X grams, grind well and mix with water or plenty of eggs. Apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to plaster joints and bones in their places, and alleviate the pain that follows, and when they use bone, and the scrape: take new wool, and its fat in broth and oil cooked, and put it on top of it.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Poultices do not heal completely, but they are better for soothing abscesses and properly treating bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plastering that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method for plastering regarding the break of bone and for alleviating the removal process from the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, ground almonds, from each take one part; and grind, mix with wine, and if the limbs are warm, mix it with wet coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method is better than the first when pus comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of visnagia, and flaxseed, balm, melilot, and marjoram, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from all take one part; and grind and mix with salt water or sweetened water or wine according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ispocrates says that for restoring strength to a broken limb, only balm made of beeswax and oil should be applied, and no other thing besides. He states that it should be soft enough between two fingers without being too sticky or too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that we should apply to the broken limb for restoration, things dried but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster for injury and pain: take mussels and offals from slaughtered animals, or bird feathers, and vervain, and milk of equal measure. Crush them, make a paste, and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, after a little while, take care that the patient doesn't feel any pain, nor is his bone of its place moved; if you don't let it heal by hand and if pain comes to the limb or itching without rest or swelling, then hasten, and let it heal, and apply the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a wet sponge, and dip them in water, and cool down the limb until the itching stops and the pain is eased; then leave the member to rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, moistened in water or oil, and fix it with a bandage, until you are sure of the presence of pus heat; and cool down the inflammation of the member, and relieve the pain, then restart the delicate healing process, and a little plaster, but don't press so hard as before; and proceed delicately until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that pus and redness, pain, swelling are present throughout the affected area, and you need to apply plaster and bandages, then restart as you did initially, in exactly the same manner.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing comes to the limb from what we have said, if it is not freed until after three days or four, five, seven; and let it not stay for any more than twenty days, according to this we see, as long as the healing progresses, approaching the fitting of the flesh up there; then you must tighten the restraint more than before, let its meat grow larger, just as I said previously; and if you see the skin dry too much than is necessary, know that maggots cannot come; take off your gloves with hot water each time you release it, and every third day, clean a little bit of the wound; through this work then cut out the maggots from the limb, hasten all that the amateur doctors do, that make the member remain twisted: this is bad, and these are unpleasant operations, and I see nothing else than to rest and operate straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	through various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of fractures exist, and various shapes. Their causes are distinct; for there are fractures made by the impact of a sword, and necks break all the bone up to where flesh begins over the bone, like in axe wounds or pike marks. Thus, this way of fracture is named "axe-breaking".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing it, this kind of fracture is called "absolute" or "clean"; and these are either large or small injuries caused by such fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack in the bone, or through stone, or on stone, or other similar cases.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that reaches up to the ligament surrounding the bone, or above the bone, and this injury can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there's a wound that goes deep into the bone as thin as hair, and has small fractures, this kind of fracture is named "hairline"; and when there's an injury caused by striking with stone or falling or something similar, causing part of the bone to break off inside it, like blacksmiths do during hammering on the pots; if a piece of the bone comes out internally.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This happens more in people with wet bones, like children's heads; it occurs through all these ways of fractures where small fragments are released, such as in cases of explosion injuries; I will speak about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all methods of breaking through by taking away from them, and the examination of attempts, and by the putrid matter which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is known when one has exposed the bone and rubs it inside, for then you open the black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the breakage, beware of the bad occurrences due to the malady, and if you see no harmful accident such as vomiting bile, loss of appetite, stretching, dizziness, fever, or other symptoms in various conditions, then there is no certainty for recovery.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming accident and hope for salvation, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the knuckle first comes to you, and it's in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the start of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh around the bone becomes rotten, and accidents occur as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the breakage of the bone reaches to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary for you to cut the broken part like this: and when you take hold of the unbroken side of the skull, and uncover upon the bone in all ways possible, and upon the appearance of injury as much as possible, and if blood discharge aids in revealing the bone, or pus accumulates, use whatever is appropriate to assist, and ensure that the area is filled with moistened cloths in oil rose. And let the wound rest until the pus accumulation subsides, and until you are sure of no further blood discharge; then begin to cut through the bone as follows: one method is that you shape it from a narrow trim ahead, and this is its form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several sizes of incisions, some narrow and others broad, all with points, made from metal and work them gently, making sure not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is out and hard, it is necessary that you pierce inside it, in such a way that you apply cuts with needles, not completely but so that they do not penetrate beyond the bone at all times; and there should be an opening or circumference of about 1 inch above the point where no part of the needle can pass through the bone. And you must have more than one, so that each goes into its place of the thickness of the bone, in such a way that you have needles for all sides; and this is the form of three types of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the broken bone is that you place one needle on the bone and turn with your hands until you know that the bone has been pierced. Then move the needle elsewhere a little after, and do this throughout; then cut along the incisors of the gap between the bones where they are apart, and do it more finely than possible and gently, as we have said, until you can pull the bone to your hand or any tool you have like forceps, and be sure not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut through the bone, it is fitting for you to remove the bone which was left in the hole from one piece of metal tool resembling a fang, but this tool should be more rigid and finer than another fang; and if there remains nothing of small bones or no scales, gently scrape them with these tools. Then treat the wound using ointments and remedies that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of operating is this, as Galen stated, which is safer; and the knife should be quite strong, for it's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you should uncover a portion of the bone, where the fracture opens and moves, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision, as described here.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, and let the area be divided into two parts, so that you are cutting towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer somewhat above, so that you gently touch all of the bone, and take great care of the cloth which is around; if it sticks to the bone, touch it lightly as well because you will not cause damage or pain when touching the bone.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not go all the way through the membrane, and only part of the bone is cut above, with small fragments remaining, it's necessary to clean up any roughness afterwards. Use a thin razor for removing scales that you should have in different quantities, so as to apply the most suitable treatment in each case according to the treatise and the nature of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you're facing large razors and then even finer ones, don't stop doing this until it's done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other kind of hair trimming and fine breakage, you must apply the treatment according to its location; this is something that cannot be left to anyone who has devoted their studies to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the scab is revealed, then it's necessary that you apply a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in olive oil, and place it on the wound; then take another double cloth, soaked in wine and olive oil, and place it over the first cloth; do this as gently as possible, so as not to weigh down the scab, then apply another bandage from above, without pulling too hard that it only touches the wound; leave it like this for one or two days, until the pus has calmed down, then remove the bandages and administer medicines such as lily roots, wheat flour, incense powder, and wormwood, and similar things; make a powder from these things, apply it to the wound, and then administer further painless medicated substances; and guard that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor let it stick together in clumps, because when clumps of clotted blood accumulate under the cloth near the brain, they will spread and infect, causing great harm to the patient; for when you place something pungent on the scab, it irritates from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Then take care, so if no accidents happen to the patient, as we have said, if there is a doubt it should not be doubted.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if nausea only comes out because of the medicine we have put on, and that virtue is as expected, then it should be that you take part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and one drachm of glue, and you place this mixture on your stomach; then you should treat with treatments as they are supposed to be treated, until it becomes healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two nasal parts above or beneath which is broken once, or only one by itself, because they are two bones; and this lower part is cartilaginous, it does not break at all, even if forced or twisted, then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it should be that you pinch your little finger or press at the inside of your nose and place the break equal within your index finger, and outwards through the nostril, until the nose regains its natural shape; and do this gently, and beware not to cause pain to the patient with your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose, and cannot come to the nostril, you should place it even with the tip of a reed slightly thicker.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, redo this procedure, and hurry to restore it on the first day if you can; should that not be possible, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has settled down, then pinch the nose tip with linestitched cloths, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you should bring up two others from the other side, if the break is there; and make them so large that they fill the hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorative requires us to anoint the wounds with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I believe it is not quite right, but it should be that the wounds are moistened in the preparation of an egg yolk mixture, and with powder from a mill; then leave the wound until the bone is hard and the cartilage is toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And in each instance use goose feathers instead of tents, and if you have one egg worth of dressing to cover it completely, then keep the wound clean, letting air pass through; simply do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come up to the nose as you work on them, then apply a poultice or wet cotton in oil, or a pinch of lavender oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses break out, then apply a plaster to the outside, made of silk meal and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk. Then place this on light cloths, do not bind it too tightly; and if the bones are broken into small pieces and are broken in many parts, then use tools suitable for that purpose, then cut along the wound, and treat everything that can harden or join together, like plasters and ointments suited to this task; and if there is no wound inside the bone, then treat the wounds, and put onions on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	regarding the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured and there's no wound at the surface, and only the breakage is outside completely, not broken into two parts but rather split internally within, one can easily identify it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary; if the breakage is in the right part, you should bend your index finger into the mouth towards the sore area; and if the breakage is in the left jawbone, you should bend your index finger of the right hand instead, and gently press on the breakage internally, and then proceed to the other hand by pushing it outward, and place them evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jawbone extends for two inches, then it is necessary that you apply an extension of two inches until they are even.
