Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth occur, or rupture, then you should restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk. Then place on the broken mandible plaster, and place on one piece two folded cloths; and place on that cloth a large flag made well, or a piece of leather equal in size to the mandible, and stick it on as best you can, and command the patient to rest, and consume light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, or that it loosens by the third day, and then set back what has changed; and apply plaster, mixing with powder from the mill with plenty of eggs or flour of yolk, after you have removed the plaster; and place on the plaster light wool, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, let it be until they are healed. Many times heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses appear, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a breakage and wound together, reward any piece of the bone that has been removed; so much skill is required for the extraction tools suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, if it is large, cover the wound with one dressing suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	by strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks many times before reaching the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: when it is broken and removed cleanly with two parts, and there are pieces left, making it easier to restore; or when there's a break accompanied by an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the veins are such that when there is a break accompanied by an injury, you have two assistants, so that one feels for the shoulder where force has broken; and the other extends to the neck towards the affected part. Then equalize the break with your hands, so that the shape should be as it should be, without any appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sponge under the shoulder and towards the hairline, it should be large according to your needs; stretch out the force (possibly referring to surgical instruments), secure the sponge in hand, so that you can equally apply pressure with your hands, as necessary.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head from the strength at the back due to it coming in front, then it is necessary for the patient to lie on their shoulder blade and put half an armpit under them, and push the shoulder down until the bone of the strength lifts.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the break in your fingers, and if you find debris inside, it is necessary to cut through it; and pull the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join with any leverage, cut into one of the incisions you have made. But place this tool against the strength so that it can ward off the syphilitic affection:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It appears like a spoon, and is not found inside, and it is as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the operation; and has two heads, as you see, and one is broad, and the other narrow, just as the wound would look when you have treated the bones; and once you are certain about extracting pus from each, if you cut the wound, and if the wound opening is small, or if you doubt about pus extraction, you should fill the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if there are several incisions, moisten them; apply oil rose and wine, and place them.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The breaking of the bone, when it involves injuries and cutting operations, is as follows: you place on the bone the plaster of the powder from the mill and some yolk of egg, and put light cloths above, and if needed, place one pole under the broken area; then take a very large band about a palm wide, and place this double cloth above the poles, and plaster it. Then take a small rod about three fingers in width and length, wrap it around the bandage so that only its ends are hanging down; and place the stick over the fracture site, turn the bandage upwards to join under the collarbone, and right above the clean spot, also above the broken spot; and then tighten each part of it, once you see that the ligament holds the fracture tightly in position, and you clearly see that the stick does not move on top of the broken bone, then give it a break for each day, and when the stitches are removed, keep it tight; have the patient lie with their back towards the wound, and if they sleep, place the small pillow under the collarbone to lift up the shoulder; to alleviate the pressure from muscle power onto the force of the injury, or if you need to tie the arm around the neck, do not release them unless there's any bad accidents happening, until at least 20 days have passed; then reapply the plaster if needed and keep it tight in this manner until it heals; and it usually takes about 28 days for healing, but less time might be needed in certain cases.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	A dislocation occurs when the shoulder breaks or is separated either at its end or in the middle, and it remains dislocated only due to impact; according to the shape of the breakage you align the shoulder and reset it according to its natural form in all possible ways. Then sprinkle on the shoulder with a flour from the mill mixed with plenty of egg whites, apply light ointments, place two layers of bandage over it; then place a large and subtle stick slightly wider than the shoulder, such that there are no parts of the shoulder underneath it. Cover this stick entirely with linen needles so the stick sits evenly; then bind it tightly into one large bandage, ensuring the stick does not move from its position, check on each day; every time it loosens, you tighten again and keep the stick even if it is displaced by force, place the patient's side under them; and the shoulder is restored after 20 days or 25. And when this number is fulfilled, you let them go loose, be sure as it is not bone that is put lightly in place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone comes forward before the socket and is not under its usual place, you should do this for the shoulder dislocation to ease abscesses that are bursting.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bones are broken at most once in the middle, but this happens rarely. But they often break at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it bends away from its original position, the patient experiences great pain and lack of movement, dizziness, and suddenly, and by chance, vomits blood, and opens up the joints in the broken bones, and one feels this well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the restoration, it should be that the patient lies on their back, and you place one and a half cushions between their shoulders, then press the shoulders, and unite the rib cages of both ribs with your hands, and skillfully fit them in all possible ways until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place plaster and bandages over the subtle salted point, or another light substance, and wrap it in a piece of cloth, and secure it on the broken bone so that it does not move. Then turn the bandage around to fit the back and tighten slightly, and reward each hour with the string, and if it loosens, then tighten; and if necessary, remove it due to corrosion or itching that occurs at the site, or pain or abscess, act quickly and remove it, and dress as you have come with treatments for this situation. Then redo the plaster until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	On the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs occurs only in strong blows to the back and within the chest, and they break due to their flexibility; and one feels this well during interrogation at the side.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And for restoration, you should place the break equal, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and hold in place with one hand, if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of ribs is located inside, the patient feels extreme pain and sharp stabbing sensations, like tears, because the bone presses against the muscle; they have a fever, vomiting and sudden large bleeding, it's distressing health-wise, and the old ones used to apply strong remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is appropriate to administer meat which inflates the belly, in order to drive away the indigestion externally.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not follow this advice, for abscesses and pus do not come about, if they have not already occurred.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has already happened, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that none of us uses suction cups on the body, in order to draw out forms, and this is similar to reason; nevertheless, there's doubt whether the suction cup draws away excesses from the body due to the weakness of position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that when covering the wound with wet wool in hot oil, and set strips between the ribs to make even the width inside, then do the treatment with the mustard poultice, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that cannot be endured by the bone piercing through the skin, and there is doubt with the patient, it may be necessary to cut at its rib under the broken bone, and one must place an instrument inside for support; then you must cut into the bone, gently drain, and then stitch the two edges of the wound, if it's large, and treat with plaster until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they come to incisions bleeding, place wet cloths in rose oil over them, and place this on the head; and cleanse as necessary for incisions, and have guards standing beside the affected area where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Regarding the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No breakage comes to the bones of the neck, and there is no bending; similarly with the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will heal or not, be on guard if you see their hands softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick their hands with a needle, if you don't feel anything.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	You know that death can occur in many ways, and if they are silent and feel well when you hold them still and not, you know that the bone's joint is saved, and that the wounds have been healed, provided a cure has been applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if something like this happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is sound or not, take care that its joints are softened, and that the events happening in touch with them, and upward wind and expulsion against will on the back; and when it has been observed on its belly, then an expulsion happens against will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is sewn on its back and it wants to rise, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that they are mortal: if you do not care for them in their treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if such events do not occur to him, then it is a simpler matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is such that you should remove any abscess if there is one, if you place oil on the spine or on egg yolk, until it eases; then place one of the restorative plasters and let it dry, and bind with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where they feel pain, until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bones are dislocated, it is necessary to cover them with the elbow; and remove the bone, then align the two edges of the wound, if it's large, with a stitch, then treat with an ointment that binds well until it heals; and if there are dislocated pieces of bone, which are called "dislocations of the knee", you should place your left hand pouch over your right hand, and hold them evenly at your power level, then apply the plaster and heat as needed; then compress, and if any bones have been dislodged, place them again, and set them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the breaking of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if this occurs, there might be a slight pain at the thigh; it extends longly, declines towards the knee, comes to the patient's discomfort in their leg, pain, and makes what is broken swell.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And in the restoration, you should extend your hand upwards as long as it is over the broken part; and understand where the break occurred and its shape. If the break happened only at the thigh, apply an even breakage there, until it reaches its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break extends along the leg or inward towards the body, guide the patient so that they lie on their belly, as long as it takes for you to properly heal this break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, place it on a plaster, then put on a stick or a reed stand, and hold the wound steady so that it doesn't move; and apply the skin over the ribs until the wound is evenly aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on their back or on their side.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscesses drain themselves, do not disturb them until the abscesses have drained fully, and then apply what we have previously mentioned. Then return to the treatment plan, and hold it accordingly without any bad accidents happening; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	regarding the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The assistants are those that are between the blade and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of these two methods: of which one is that you take a solid stick of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two pieces of cloth together, and bend them up, then place the patient's broken arm on top of one seat; then pour the broken part over the stick until it reaches the elbow, and has made half a turn with the length of the stick, then bend over any heavy object or let assistants hold it downwards; then put the pieces of cloth so that the break is evenly between their hands, until the broken part returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you place the patient on their back, and tie their hand to their neck, then command two assistants such that one shaves the area where there is the break with their hands, and the other cuts off any excess at every inch, and extend each person to their own side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then restrain it during the operation and during the operation itself, and extend each of your assistants to their respective positions.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the operation is near the head of the shoulder, you should place one band in front and the other towards the knife during the operation, under the wound; similarly, if the operation is opposite the knife, you should gently place your hands without effort until the wound matches up on both sides. Then evenly cut the wound, as it should be, and hold it together, unless pus comes out from the bandages.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if pus comes out, do not restrain too tightly for up to seven days, and place wet wool in a comfortable position with rose oil, until the pus at the bottom is relieved; then restrain it, and the way to restrain should be that you place the plaster over the cut. Then join the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; apply the cloth, and hold tightly on the shoulder and arm, so that the arm is in its usual position, without anything preventing it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt whether the bone is moving, use elbows and place a larger and stronger wedge between each cut than the others, leaving an inch of space between each wedge. Each wedge should be large enough to pass three inches on each side of the cut; then hold the wedges in place as I instructed at the beginning of this chapter on cutting, more strongly without pulling away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the base of the nails and the constriction, as we have said, when you restore a broken limb, and if there is doubt about discharging pus, leave it to be bound for seven days, as we have said; then examine every three days the binding, ensuring no itchiness spreads or grows at the site, or that ulcers do not come upon the limb because it's too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If there is the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such incidents occur, or if the healing takes longer than three days or more, and the patient feels better lying on their back, with hands on their stomach; and place beneath the shoulder an inch of wool evenly spread, and every hour or so during the day, observe whether the shape of the broken limb doesn't move or isn't softened by the bandages; if the address, through the virtue of medicine, and gives meat as we have placed before it in such a manner that the meat becomes at first refined; and when they begin to recover, if it is full.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg must be in place for 40 days; and then one should loosen them, take baths, and administer ointment medications to sooth the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and tangled, it must be left to loosen for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones which are called the 'foscile' pair. One bone is small and it forms the socket; the other is larger and it is beneath the small one towards the back of the hand. By chance, only the large foscile might break, or just the smaller one, or perhaps they both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing. And when the large bones are broken, the healing is bad, and more painful than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it's only the small bone that is broken, then it should be allowed to stretch slightly and be made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's the large bone that is broken, then it should be pulled more tightly; and extend on his left side, and elevate the sleeve of his hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the other bones, and let the patient bend towards himself, with the left side in front of him higher than the others so that no discomfort arises to the body; then spread out the assistants' arms below his shoulder or elbow, and another set of assistants above on the other side.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the eyes evenly, according to their best form.

And if in the breakage into pieces, you place each back in its position, and if there is none of them that grabs the knee, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut through and the bone, as we have said before.

And if during the beginning of the restoration pus comes out, then prepare a bandage made from roset oil and white beeswax, ensuring it's neither too hard nor too soft; and tie this bandage skillfully upwards until the inflamed pus-filled areas have calmed.

Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand

Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and after the flesh feels great pain, know that it has not been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Do so that it is in its place, then smear the wound with a black vinegar bandage, and properly if it's in the right position; and don't put anything like plaster or other substance on the wound where there is oil, to prevent any infection or corruption from occurring. Then administer the remedies after you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover it completely according to the size of the wound, making sure that the wound is not squeezed with force; many times people did this and caused either death or corrosion on the flesh once; and make the compresses softer and more soothing than other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that an accident may have occurred there, as we said, and you find pain in the limb, it does not seem appropriate to apply hot stones; but wrap around, instead of hot stones, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the blisters have appeared on the wound, remove what you have placed with all the wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as tetracrm药物 and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary for you to dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it has healed and become healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be put together so that the joint moves easily forward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the joints continue to do this for days and it cannot be sewn but remains like that with the joint, know that there are small bone fragments causing this issue. Therefore, you need to work on the wound with a tented method, and remove all these pieces of bone that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a sinus tract comes to the limb or any other form of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what he has explained in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open in the limb, like the bones of the knee or shoulder, or other large joints, do not treat it immediately because many die from this. Instead, let it heal naturally until it withers; sometimes it will drain on its own after about twenty to thirty days. Then you can treat the wound if possible. If you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The burns often come after rubbing with the breeze, especially near the joints. A terrible thing to see is how the limb's shape changes; and by chance cannot perform its natural actions on it.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then when it is fresh: if you administer stictch medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, sarsagot, carageen, and similar others, do so according to whichever of these you desire or all together, mixing them with stictch wine or with the yolk of an egg or with honey; then apply it on a nut in poultices, bind it well, and don't remove it with your hands for days; afterwards displace it, and start another poultice until the swellings are removed; or you bind onto a well-made piece of cork because the properties of cork are such that they remove all swellings from limbs; if the swelling has turned into hardness like stone and needs to be removed, cover it with a paste, making the excess visible; or take it off with no one's help until it is removed, and treat it until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb that becomes weak after being garrisoned
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breakage of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens through various causes: because one was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many ties, and could not bring circulation to the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to large movements not in their time; or because they have little blood in their body, if they are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you should eat the herb in him, and make the body tender until there are numerous effects within him; then provide baths for him, and give him joy and rest. Afterward, apply ointment to the limb, so that the ointment attracts towards the main circulation, and washes with hot water repeatedly until the circulation matches the limb; and restores his natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If a limb is bent after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the bone is broken apart, though the form of the limb is ugly, it does not lose its natural function: nor should you believe those who say one must break the entire limb anew. And many foolish people have done this in our land; these practices are condemned, causing great harms and even death. However, if the inflammation and torture are still fresh, then it's right to immerse them in hot water, or to cook mollifying herbs such as leaves of basil, roots, and mallow, among similar remedies; and apply one liter of a moistening plaster, such as well-made yarrow extract, and take the basil oil, mix it with tallow or nut oil, and apply the plaster over that. Alternatively, you can take greased figs, grind them with cinnamon powder, and other medicines that soften heat, and then make a plaster from these.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time does one remove the node by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement of the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is old and hardened, like bone, and requires treatment with metal tools, then it might be necessary to operate up to the bone, gently on the delicate incision; and incorporate patience and careful consideration in the healing process.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, for this reason it cannot move, and the limbs are misaligned, causing patients to experience great pain and severe injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation happens without a cause and if it is about to occur now, you should bring it back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if you delay, they will swell and perhaps even pierce the bones at their joints; in this case it is not suitable to move them every hour when they are swollen: it can bring pus and other pains many times. Nevertheless, whenever this happens, send for a surgeon, then leave him alone until the abscess subsides completely. Then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently manipulate it, and treat each member as if it is where you are accustomed to treating them.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters about the dislocations of the shoulder up to here.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws become dislocated forwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are slightly ossified at their joints and somewhat soft; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, causing saliva from the mouth to escape that they cannot contain it, nor can they close their mouth, and wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And when it is complete and done, you must quickly remove the dislocation, without hesitation. Do this with such skill that your assistants cut near the head of the patient, and insert a sharp instrument in her mouth at the root of the dislocated jawbone if the dislocation involves two parts; and the other hand should be used to push the other end out from under the chin, aiming for equilibrium. Instruct the patient to soften her jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And push the thumb until it is balanced, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if bringing it back hurts, likewise when the two jaws are together, use hot water and oil, until you gently reset them; do not overly force their return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought evenly back, and the mouth of the patient closes well after being mollified, place moist cloths in a poultice made from rose oil and beeswax, then tie them loosely with oily threads; have the patient lie on their back, and let their head be between two pillows, so that it doesn't move to either side nor try to twist, but only consume light food until the pains are eased, and the jaws are closed. And then have them eat lightly, without working their mouth open for eating or drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be properly aligned within an hour and are not yet fully restored to their original position, it leads to fevers becoming habituated and recurrent, and in consequence stomach discomfort or even vomiting occurs.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times, death befalls the one who encounters this within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the fortress
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strength cannot relieve from within the ribcage and the back, and it is relieved once outside, and well can one feel this.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in this treatment, the patient lies on their back and extends their arms. Then press the body into the shape of your palm, and they will return to that position; then apply plaster and bind them tightly together, and strain the shoulder blade. The neck which is opposite the cut cannot dislocate; if it does, one must reposition it back into place, as we have said. Then apply plaster and bind it again, and strain it, instructing the patient to rest until they are healed. Thus similarly, the shoulders of the spine will be returned when it has been freed from its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Regarding the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: One way it is dislocated from the part under the armpit towards the back. The second way is at the base of the heel; and by chance dislocated at the top part, this happens rarely; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and several times dislocated from below toward the armpit, even in those with little flesh, because at these jumps it happens quickly; in those with enough flesh, a jump occurs and returns within the bones.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men from impact or breaking, and the shoulder swells with an acute abscess, and they think it is dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must prove it, as long as you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that when it is directed towards the armpit, there's a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one; you will find their differences clearly expressed. You'll discover a hollow at the top of the shoulder and from under the armpit to the collarbone, as if it were an 'o'; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to his nose or move it in any way. Also, if it's dislocated upwards, it's not hidden either; because you find it clearly at the collarbone. And this type of dislocation can't be reversed until it's new, or when the child is born.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And this method is that the minister lifts the hand away from the ill part at the top, then places his thumbs on the joint and raises the joint to force up at its place; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upwards, putting it back in position; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it doesn't come about as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and give them restorative and soothing treatment, such as decoctions of thyme, fenugreek, and marjoram in hot water, and administer this treatment. Then wrap the patient's back with the same fabric on which you have placed their head, put a cushion under their armpit that is neither too soft nor too hard; then place the hand underneath their heel, lift their shoulder blade upwards forcefully, pull their hand down towards their body; and other assistants scrape the top of your patient's shoulder blade until it no longer moves; this shoulder now returns immediately. If you see that you have reset it in this way: and know that there should be someone larger than your patient present at home when this is done; and stand straight opposite the armpit, support their shoulder under the cushion near the shoulder blade, lift the cushion up so that the patient hangs down into an inverted 'V'; and other assistants pull the hand towards the belly of the patient as it goes back.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the organs are too light, they can move with anything heavy, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And resetting it can also be done in other ways: and you bury the long stake in the ground, so that the joint is held as firmly as a pistol, but not too thick or too slippery; then place it under the organ, but make sure there's a layer of fat underneath, and the organ remains long along the length of the stake; then extend your hand from the other side downwards, forming the connection will return to its place quickly; and if it does not return with all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick of two arms wide and four inches thick, which has the head rounded to fit through the fat on one side directly into the joint, according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie it on the end of the rod covered with skin underneath, so that the rod does not hurt the hair, then place it against the skin from where you are to enter smoothly all around; and extend your arm along the rod from head to toe, and tie the shoulder on the rod, and the arm at the wrist, then put the arm on one of two long sticks about as wide, and keep the hand extended downward, and leave the body hanging from another side: the joint will return immediately now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is thus, in whatever way it may be, if need be you should put on the saddle a thread that's even, then place the plastered substance with mill-ground powder, along with incense and egg yolk, over the whole shoulder and around it, then remove from the saddle addition, and tie up the bandage onto the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain in such a way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is necessary that he eats moderately, until the limbs are reinforced, for it will heal faster; and then eat more after five days or seven, and move them; and if it's firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has moved due to moisture that has come upon it or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply three cauterizations to it, as was explained in our chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint doesn't hold, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint would never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations in the buttocks area and breasts or rearward, are caused by pushing and stretching of hands, and performed at other locations; and treat until they heal properly.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes redness to the limb, and persistent movements, then use hot baths many times, until that redness disappears and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder has been dislocated at its points, and returns to them; and if it's dislocated from all sides, as well as in front and behind, and dislocations are not responsive because one can see and feel them clearly; and is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the metal blade with your hand, if you can see it clearly.

Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated right away, it should be made to lie down straight and held by the assistant's hands behind the leg, over the ankle. Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then again with your left, twice each, after which extend it up high, firmly keeping the foot upwards; do this twice as instructed before. If it returns, that is good; if not, start again with the process, because it will return; and if it cannot return in such a way, make the person lie down so their back is towards the ground and plant firmly between their buttocks, tying it tightly to hold them together, preventing injury to their ankle. Then take turns attending each assistant's hands, or another one cuts the healthy leg above where the dislocation occurred, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it reaches the point, then place the plaster and bandage on top, apply firm pressure, and hold it in place, bind the foot to the leg, and watch that the ligaments behind the ankle are not too tight; let it be for two or three days, and if they loosen, remove them. Then release after three days or a quarter of a week, and guide the patient for another four days; and if he progresses beyond this point, it is not certain that he will still dislocate.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pus-filled areas have come out, you should soothe them as we have said elsewhere, until they are cleansed.
des dois	From these two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two shoulders are dislocated, if they suit to be beautifully extended in work, and it is a slight matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in neither the neck nor the foot, you must have the patient sit straight on one side or right on a table completely flat, and put your foot on whatever extends from these joints. Press with your foot until it feels relieved; when it's even and nothing pops out, place a stool under the ball of your foot for about two shoulders, then apply firm pressure, and leave it for three days, then release him; and have him rest until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	On surgery and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you need to restore it, many times death occurs: if not being presumptuous in the treatment, if you are not knowledgeable in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, then do not be bold; start by soothing things like pus extraction initially, and leave the patient to God's mercy, if you do not see hope of recovery; when you do see hope, immediately reset the limb in place, just as pus extraction and healing should progress; when the limb is in place, administer soothing pus extraction remedies, treat the wound according to its nature, with dried ointments; and if there are fractures along with dislocation, and small bones have broken off, set them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; be cautious of falling into fear's path as I've stated before, for this will cause you harm according to your Creator, and use your knowledge and body's skills wisely.
